Istihsan Overrides Qiyas: The Ruling on Mistakenly Slaughtering Another's Udhiyah
Ruling with proof: istihsan vs qiyas on mistaken slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling (sahih, no guarantee) when two persons mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah, explain the reasoning of istihsan based on implicit permission, and contrast it with the qiyas position of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Customary delegation makes the slaughter valid – istihsan overrides strict qiyas when the owner would naturally consent.

What happens if two people at Eid each accidentally slaughter the other's sacrificial animal? Strict analogy might say it's invalid, but Hanafi fiqh uses istihsan to uphold the sacrifice. In this lesson, we examine the core case and the powerful legal reasoning behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
Read the first part of the passage: 'ولو غلطا وذبح كل أضحية صاحبه صح ولا يضمنان وهذا استحسان'. Identify the scenario and the Hanafi position.
The ruling is that the sacrifice is valid (sahih) and no guarantee (damān) is required.
2
Compare with the qiyas position
The text then presents the qiyas: a valid sacrifice is not achieved and each must guarantee. This is attributed to Imam Zufar. Note the logical elements of qiyas: the original case (asl) of slaughtering another's sheep without permission, the new case (far'), and the common cause (illa).
The qiyas position is not the mufta bihi; it is presented for contrast.
3
Analyze the wajh of istihsan
The text gives the reasoning (wajh) for istihsan: the animals are designated for slaughter during specified days; the owner customarily does not slaughter himself; time is limited; thus implicit permission (idhn dilalah) is established. List each point.
This reasoning overrides the illa of 'trespass' because the owner's delegation is assumed.
4
Understand the concept of implicit permission (idhn dilalah)
The passage compares this to a butcher tying a sheep's legs – the owner's silence and the urgency imply consent. Also compares to fasting and issues of ihram by proxy. Grasp how custom and necessity can create legal permission without explicit words.
This is a key principle in Hanafi fiqh, especially in muamalat and ibadat where time is constrained.
5
Apply the dispute map
Use the madhhab dispute map to clearly separate the positions: Hanafi majority (istihsan) vs. Zufar (qiyas). Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) and which is mufta bihi.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, not inter-madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله تعالى: (ولو غلطا وذبح كل أضحية صاحبه صح ولا يضمنان وهذا استحسان والقياس أنه لا تجوز الأضحية ويضمن كل واحد منهما لصاحبه وهو قول زفر رحمه الله تعالى لأنه متعد بالذبح بغير أمره فيضمن كما إذا ذبح شاة اشتراها القصاب والتضحية قربة فلا تتأدى بنية غيره. وجه الاستحسان أنها تعينت للذبح لتعينها بالأضحية حتى وجب عليه أن يضحي بها بعينها في أيام النحر، ويكره أن يبدل بها غيرها فصار المالك مستعيناً بمن يكون أهلاً للذبح فصار مأذوناً له دلالة لأنها تفوت بمضي هذه الأيام ويخاف أن يعجز عن إقامتها العارض يغتريه فصار كما إذا ذبح شاة وشد القصاب رجليها وكيف لا يأذن له وفيه مسارعة إلى الخير وتحقيق ما عينه ولا يبالي بفوات مباشرته وشهوده لحصول ما هو أعظم من ذلك وهو ما بيناه فيصير اذناً دلالة وهو كالصوم، ومن هذا الجنس مسائل استحسانية لأصحابنا ذكرناها في الإحرام عن الغير. ثم إذا جاز ذلك عنهما يأخذ كل واحد منهما أضحيته إن كانت باقية ولا يضمنه لأنه وكيله، فإن كان كل واحد منهما أكل ما ذبحه تحلل كل واحد منهما صاحبه فيجزئه لأنه لو أطعمه الكل في الابتداء يجوز، وإن كان غنياً فكذا له أن يحلل في الانتهاء، وإن تشاحا كان لكل واحد منهما أن يضمن صاحبه قيمة لحمه ثم يتصدق بتلك القيمة لأنه بدل عن اللحم أنقص من فصار كما لو باع أضحية غيره كان الحكم ما ذكرناه. وذكر في المحيط مطلقاً من غير قيد فقال : ذبح أضحية غيره بلا أمره جاز استحساناً ولا يضمن لأنه في العرف لا يتولى صاحب الأضحية ذبحها بنفسه بل يفوض إلى غيره فصار مأذوناً دلالة كالقصاب إذا شد رجل شاة للذبح فذبحها إنسان بغير أمره لا يضمن ولو باع أضحية واشترى بثمنها غيرها فإن كان الثاني الأول تصدق بالفضل، ولو غصب شاة وضحى بها جاز عن أضحيته لأنه ملكها بالغصب السابق بخلاف ما لو كانت وديعة لأنه يضمنها بالذبح فلم يثبت له الملك إلا بعده. ولو ذبح أضحية غيره بغير أمره عن نفسه، فإن ضمنه المالك قيمتها تجوز عن الذابح دون المالك لأنه ظهر أن الإراقة حصلت على ملكه على ما بينا في المغصوبة، وإن أخذها مذبوحة أجزأت المالك عن التضحية لأنه قد نواها فلا يضره ذبحها غيره على ما بينا.
He (the author) said: (And if they make a mistake and each one slaughters the sacrifice of his companion, it is valid and they do not guarantee each other. This is istihsan. The qiyas is that the sacrifice is not valid and each one must guarantee the companion's animal, which is the saying of Zufar, because he is a trespasser by slaughtering without his permission, so he guarantees, just as if he slaughters a sheep that a butcher bought. And the sacrifice is an act of worship, so it is not performed by the intention of another. The wajh of istihsan is that the animals are designated for slaughter because they are determined for the udhiyah, so he must sacrifice that very animal on the days of Nahr, and it is disliked to replace it with another. So the owner becomes one who seeks help from someone qualified for slaughter, so he is implicitly authorized, because the opportunity is lost with the passing of these days, and he fears the inability to perform it due to an obstacle. So it is like when a person slaughters a sheep and a butcher ties its legs. How could he not authorize him? And there is hastening to good and fulfilling what he determined, and he does not mind missing direct action and witnessing because of obtaining something greater, which we have explained. So it becomes an implicit authorization, like fasting. And this category includes istihsani issues from our companions, which we mentioned in the section on ihram by proxy. Then, when it is valid from both, each one takes his sacrifice if it remains, and he does not guarantee, because he is his agent. If each one ate what he slaughtered, each one seeks dissolution from his companion, and it suffices, because if he had fed him the entire animal initially, it would be permissible. And if he is wealthy, likewise he may dissolve at the end. If they dispute, each one may demand from his companion the value of the meat, then give charity with that value, because it is a substitute for the meat that is less than... So it becomes like selling another's sacrifice, the ruling is as we mentioned. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit unconditionally: he said: If one slaughters another's sacrifice without his permission, it is valid by istihsan and he does not guarantee, because customarily the owner does not slaughter it himself but delegates to another, so he is implicitly authorized, like the butcher if he ties a sheep for slaughter and another person slaughters it without permission, he does not guarantee. And if he sells a sacrifice and buys another with its price, if the second is better than the first, he gives charity with the excess. And if he usurps a sheep and sacrifices it, it is valid for his udhiyah because he owned it by prior usurpation, unlike if it was a trust, because then he guarantees by slaughtering, so ownership does not occur except after that. And if he slaughters another's sacrifice without permission for himself, then if the owner guarantees its value, it is valid for the slaughterer, not the owner, because it appears that the blood was shed on his property, as we explained in the case of a usurped animal. And if the owner takes it slaughtered, it suffices for his sacrifice, because he intended it, so his slaughter by another does not harm him, as we explained.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This is a major istihsani ruling in Hanafi fiqh. The case: two people each mistakenly slaughter the other's designated udhiyah. The qiyas (supported by Zufar) says it is invalid and each must compensate because they acted without permission and worship cannot be performed with another's intention. However, the Hanafi position (istihsan) says it is valid and no compensation is needed. The reasoning: each animal is designated for slaughter and must be sacrificed within the days; the owner customarily delegates the act; time is limited; thus implicit permission (idhn dilalah) is established. The text then covers scenarios: if the meat is eaten, each must seek dissolution (tahlil) if wealthy; if they dispute, they exchange value; and other related cases like slaughtering without permission in general, usurped animals, etc. The key principle is customary delegation.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A legal method preferring a ruling different from qiyas due to stronger evidence like custom or necessity.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from an original case to a new case based on a common illa.
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi scholar known for strict adherence to qiyas.
إذن دلالة (idhn dilalah): Implicit permission inferred from circumstances, custom, or necessity rather than explicit verbal authorization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position (istihsan) in this lesson, what is the ruling when two persons mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah?
A) The sacrifice is invalid and each must guarantee the other.
B) The sacrifice is valid and no guarantee is required.
C) The sacrifice is valid only if the owners attend the slaughter.
D) The sacrifice is invalid, but no guarantee is required.

Key Takeaway
Customary delegation (idhn dilalah) validates the sacrifice when two people mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah, overriding the qiyas of trespass.

Practical Scenarios and Implicit Authorization: Further Cases of Slaughtering Another's Sacrifice
Expansion of istihsan ruling to additional scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of idhn dilalah to related scenarios: eating the mistakenly slaughtered meat, disputing over compensation, general slaughter without permission, and cases of usurped or trusted animals.

Core Idea
The principle of implicit permission extends to various derivative cases, each with a distinct ruling based on custom and intention.

The core ruling on mistaken slaughter opens the door to several practical questions: What if they eat the meat? What if they dispute? What about a person who slaughters another's animal without any mistake? In this lesson, we explore the furuat and see how the principle of idhn dilalah operates consistently across different situations.

Guided Path
1
Scenario after valid slaughter: eating the meat
Read the part: 'ثم إذا جاز ذلك عنهما يأخذ كل واحد منهما أضحيته إن كانت باقية... فإن كان كل واحد منهما أكل ما ذبحه تحلل كل واحد منهما صاحبه فيجزئه'. Understand the ruling when the meat is consumed: each owner can seek dissolution (tahlil) if the other is wealthy, or simply give charity equivalent to the meat value.
The tahlil is needed because the slaughterer consumed meat that legally belonged to the owner.
2
Dispute and compensation
Read: 'وإن تشاحا كان لكل واحد منهما أن يضمن صاحبه قيمة لحمه'. If they cannot agree, each may claim the value of the meat from the other and then give that value in charity.
This avoids unlawful consumption of another's property.
3
General rule: slaughtering another's sacrifice without permission
The passage from al-Muhit states: 'ذبح أضحية غيره بلا أمره جاز استحساناً ولا يضمن لأنه في العرف لا يتولى صاحب الأضحية ذبحها بنفسه'. This broadens the principle to any slaughter of another's sacrifice, not just mistaken exchange.
The custom of delegation is general, not limited to the swap scenario.
4
Edge cases: usurped (maghsūb) vs. trust (wadī'ah) animals
Read: 'ولو غصب شاة وضحى بها جاز عن أضحيته لأنه ملكها بالغصب السابق بخلاف ما لو كانت وديعة'. A usurper becomes owner by prior possession, so his sacrifice is valid for himself. But a trustee who slaughters a trust animal must guarantee it, so ownership only transfers after guarantee.
This distinguishes between different types of possession.
5
Intention: slaughtering for oneself vs. for the owner
Read: 'ولو ذبح أضحية غيره بغير أمره عن نفسه، فإن ضمنه المالك قيمتها تجوز عن الذابح دون المالك... وإن أخذها المالك مذبوحة أجزأت المالك'. The intention of the slaughterer matters: if he intends his own udhiyah, it becomes valid for him only if the owner guarantees; if the owner takes it as slaughtered, it becomes valid for the owner.
This shows the importance of niyyah and subsequent actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله تعالى: (ولو غلطا وذبح كل أضحية صاحبه صح ولا يضمنان وهذا استحسان والقياس أنه لا تجوز الأضحية ويضمن كل واحد منهما لصاحبه وهو قول زفر رحمه الله تعالى لأنه متعد بالذبح بغير أمره فيضمن كما إذا ذبح شاة اشتراها القصاب والتضحية قربة فلا تتأدى بنية غيره. وجه الاستحسان أنها تعينت للذبح لتعينها بالأضحية حتى وجب عليه أن يضحي بها بعينها في أيام النحر، ويكره أن يبدل بها غيرها فصار المالك مستعيناً بمن يكون أهلاً للذبح فصار مأذوناً له دلالة لأنها تفوت بمضي هذه الأيام ويخاف أن يعجز عن إقامتها العارض يغتريه فصار كما إذا ذبح شاة وشد القصاب رجليها وكيف لا يأذن له وفيه مسارعة إلى الخير وتحقيق ما عينه ولا يبالي بفوات مباشرته وشهوده لحصول ما هو أعظم من ذلك وهو ما بيناه فيصير اذناً دلالة وهو كالصوم، ومن هذا الجنس مسائل استحسانية لأصحابنا ذكرناها في الإحرام عن الغير. ثم إذا جاز ذلك عنهما يأخذ كل واحد منهما أضحيته إن كانت باقية ولا يضمنه لأنه وكيله، فإن كان كل واحد منهما أكل ما ذبحه تحلل كل واحد منهما صاحبه فيجزئه لأنه لو أطعمه الكل في الابتداء يجوز، وإن كان غنياً فكذا له أن يحلل في الانتهاء، وإن تشاحا كان لكل واحد منهما أن يضمن صاحبه قيمة لحمه ثم يتصدق بتلك القيمة لأنه بدل عن اللحم أنقص من فصار كما لو باع أضحية غيره كان الحكم ما ذكرناه. وذكر في المحيط مطلقاً من غير قيد فقال : ذبح أضحية غيره بلا أمره جاز استحساناً ولا يضمن لأنه في العرف لا يتولى صاحب الأضحية ذبحها بنفسه بل يفوض إلى غيره فصار مأذوناً دلالة كالقصاب إذا شد رجل شاة للذبح فذبحها إنسان بغير أمره لا يضمن ولو باع أضحية واشترى بثمنها غيرها فإن كان الثاني الأول تصدق بالفضل، ولو غصب شاة وضحى بها جاز عن أضحيته لأنه ملكها بالغصب السابق بخلاف ما لو كانت وديعة لأنه يضمنها بالذبح فلم يثبت له الملك إلا بعده. ولو ذبح أضحية غيره بغير أمره عن نفسه، فإن ضمنه المالك قيمتها تجوز عن الذابح دون المالك لأنه ظهر أن الإراقة حصلت على ملكه على ما بينا في المغصوبة، وإن أخذها مذبوحة أجزأت المالك عن التضحية لأنه قد نواها فلا يضره ذبحها غيره على ما بينا.
He (the author) said: (And if they make a mistake and each one slaughters the sacrifice of his companion, it is valid and they do not guarantee each other. This is istihsan. The qiyas is that the sacrifice is not valid and each one must guarantee the companion's animal, which is the saying of Zufar, because he is a trespasser by slaughtering without his permission, so he guarantees, just as if he slaughters a sheep that a butcher bought. And the sacrifice is an act of worship, so it is not performed by the intention of another. The wajh of istihsan is that the animals are designated for slaughter because they are determined for the udhiyah, so he must sacrifice that very animal on the days of Nahr, and it is disliked to replace it with another. So the owner becomes one who seeks help from someone qualified for slaughter, so he is implicitly authorized, because the opportunity is lost with the passing of these days, and he fears the inability to perform it due to an obstacle. So it is like when a person slaughters a sheep and a butcher ties its legs. How could he not authorize him? And there is hastening to good and fulfilling what he determined, and he does not mind missing direct action and witnessing because of obtaining something greater, which we have explained. So it becomes an implicit authorization, like fasting. And this category includes istihsani issues from our companions, which we mentioned in the section on ihram by proxy. Then, when it is valid from both, each one takes his sacrifice if it remains, and he does not guarantee, because he is his agent. If each one ate what he slaughtered, each one seeks dissolution from his companion, and it suffices, because if he had fed him the entire animal initially, it would be permissible. And if he is wealthy, likewise he may dissolve at the end. If they dispute, each one may demand from his companion the value of the meat, then give charity with that value, because it is a substitute for the meat that is less than... So it becomes like selling another's sacrifice, the ruling is as we mentioned. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit unconditionally: he said: If one slaughters another's sacrifice without his permission, it is valid by istihsan and he does not guarantee, because customarily the owner does not slaughter it himself but delegates to another, so he is implicitly authorized, like the butcher if he ties a sheep for slaughter and another person slaughters it without permission, he does not guarantee. And if he sells a sacrifice and buys another with its price, if the second is better than the first, he gives charity with the excess. And if he usurps a sheep and sacrifices it, it is valid for his udhiyah because he owned it by prior usurpation, unlike if it was a trust, because then he guarantees by slaughtering, so ownership does not occur except after that. And if he slaughters another's sacrifice without permission for himself, then if the owner guarantees its value, it is valid for the slaughterer, not the owner, because it appears that the blood was shed on his property, as we explained in the case of a usurped animal. And if the owner takes it slaughtered, it suffices for his sacrifice, because he intended it, so his slaughter by another does not harm him, as we explained.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This is a major istihsani ruling in Hanafi fiqh. The case: two people each mistakenly slaughter the other's designated udhiyah. The qiyas (supported by Zufar) says it is invalid and each must compensate because they acted without permission and worship cannot be performed with another's intention. However, the Hanafi position (istihsan) says it is valid and no compensation is needed. The reasoning: each animal is designated for slaughter and must be sacrificed within the days; the owner customarily delegates the act; time is limited; thus implicit permission (idhn dilalah) is established. The text then covers scenarios: if the meat is eaten, each must seek dissolution (tahlil) if wealthy; if they dispute, they exchange value; and other related cases like slaughtering without permission in general, usurped animals, etc. The key principle is customary delegation.

Key Terms
تحلل (tahlil): A mutual release or dissolution of rights, often requiring charity if the parties are wealthy.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation – taking another's property wrongfully with the intent to own, which transfers ownership with liability.
وديعة (wadi'ah): Trust – property left with another for safekeeping. The trustee does not own it.
محيط (al-Muhit): A Hanafi fiqh reference work by Imam Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani (or others), cited as authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Muhit, what is the ruling if a person slaughters another's udhiyah without any permission?
A) It is invalid and the slaughterer must guarantee the value.
B) It is valid by istihsan and no guarantee is required because of custom.
C) It is valid only if the owner was present and knew.
D) It is invalid, but the owner may choose to accept it.

Key Takeaway
The principle of idhn dilalah extends beyond mistaken exchange to any slaughter of another's udhiyah, with specific rulings for consumption, dispute, and different types of possession.

Fatwa on Dispute Over Tied Sacrificial Animals
Fatwa on ownership dispute after a mistake in tying animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two or more persons dispute ownership of a tied sacrificial animal and determine the validity of the sacrifice.

Core Idea
Disputed sacrificial animal: divided equally, sacrifice invalid for both.

What happens when two people tie their sacrificial animals together, a mix-up occurs, and they both claim one particular animal? This fatwa from Fatawa Ahwar provides a clear ruling: the disputed animal is split between them, but neither can sacrifice it. The key principle is that a valid sacrifice requires clear ownership. When ownership is ambiguous, the animal's use for 'ibadah is invalidated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Two men tie their udhiyah animals in the same place. A mistake (ghalat) leads to a dispute over one animal, each claiming it is his. Note that there is also a second animal that neither claims.
The dispute is only over one animal; the other is undisputed.
2
Ruling on the disputed animal
The judge rules that the disputed animal is divided equally between the two claimants (half each in ownership), but the sacrifice from that animal is not valid for either of them.
The division is in terms of ownership/value, not the actual slaughter for sacrifice.
3
Ruling on the undisputed animal
The animal over which there is no dispute goes to the public treasury (bayt al-mal) because it is considered lost property (mal da'i'), as its owner cannot be identified.
This applies only when both deny it or neither claims it.
4
Exception for larger animals
If the animals were camels or cows (which can be shared by multiple persons), the sacrifice is valid from all of them collectively. The size allows joint ownership without invalidating the sacrifice.
This exception highlights that the invalidity in the first case is due to the inability to share the animal for sacrifice.
5
Three-animal scenario with a defect
When three persons tie three animals, and one is found defective (invalidating its sacrifice), each denies the defective one. The defective animal goes to bayt al-mal, and the remaining two are divided into three shares (one third each to the three owners).
The same principle applies: disputed/defective animals are removed, and remaining are divided equitably.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى أهوار : رجلان ربطاً أضحيتهما في مربط ثم غلطا فتنازعا في واحدة كل منهما مدعيها ولا الأخرى يقضي بالذي تنازعا فيها بينهما نصفين ولا تجوز الأضحية عنهما بهما. وقال يدعي بعضهم : تجوز عنهما جميعاً. والصحيح الأول، والذي لم يتنازعا فيها لبيت المال لأنها مال ضائع، ولو كانت إبلاً وبقراً جازت الأضحية عنهما جميعاً، وإذا ربطوا ثلاثة أضحية في رباط واحد ثم وجدا بواحد عيباً يمنع جواز الأضحية وأنكر كل واحد منهم أن تكون له المعيبة وتنازعوا في الأخريين فالمعيبة لبيت المال لأنها مال ضائع ويقضى بينهم بالأخريين أثلاثاً ا هـ .
And in Fatawa Ahwar: Two men tied their sacrificial animals in a stable, then they made a mistake, and they disputed over one of them, each claiming it to be his, and not the other. The judge rules that the one they disputed over is between them in halves, and the sacrifice is not valid from them for either. And some claim that it is valid from both. And the correct is the first. And the one over which they did not dispute goes to the public treasury because it is a lost property. And if they were camels or cows, the sacrifice would be valid from all of them. And if three tied three sacrificial animals in one tie, then they found one defect that prevents validity, and each denied that the defective one was his, and they disputed over the other two, then the defective one goes to the public treasury, and the judge rules between them over the other two in thirds.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This fatwa deals with a dispute after a mistake. Two animals are tied, the owners make a mistake, and they dispute over one animal (each claiming it is his). The ruling: the disputed animal is divided equally (half and half), but the sacrifice is not valid for either because ownership is unclear. The other animal (the one not disputed) goes to bayt al-mal because it is a lost property (mal da'i'). For camels or cows, the sacrifice is valid because they can be shared amicably. In a case with three animals and a defective one, the defective one goes to bayt al-mal, and the remaining two are divided in thirds among the three owners.

Key Terms
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Islamic state, which receives ownerless or unclaimed property.
مال ضائع (mal da'i'): Lost property; an asset whose owner is unknown or unclaimed.
أضحية (udhiyah): A sacrificial animal slaughtered during Eid al-Adha.
ربط (rabbata): To tie; here, to tether animals together in one place.
غلط (ghalat): Mistake; unintentional error leading to confusion.
تنازع (tanazu'): Dispute; each party claiming ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa from Ahwar, what happens to the animal over which two owners dispute?
A) It is divided equally and the sacrifice is valid for both.
B) It is divided equally but the sacrifice is not valid for either.
C) It goes to the public treasury.
D) It is given to the one who denies it.

Key Takeaway
When ownership of a tied sacrificial animal is disputed, the animal is divided equally among claimants but cannot be sacrificed; if no one claims it, it goes to the public treasury, except for camels and cows where joint sacrifice is valid.

Sacrificing Another's Animal: Custom, Istihsan, and Liability
Series of rulings on sacrificing another's animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sacrificing another's animal in various scenarios and apply the principle of istihsan based on custom (urf) to determine validity and liability.

Core Idea
Custom (urf) can grant implicit permission, making sacrifice of another's animal valid without liability.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a set of rulings on udhiyah involving animals belonging to others. The Hanafi school relies on istihsan (juridical preference) and custom to resolve these cases. Understanding these rulings will deepen your appreciation of how usul principles like istihsan and idhn dilalah (implicit permission) function in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Start with the ruling from al-Muhit: slaughtering another's sacrificial animal without permission is valid (ja'iz) by istihsan and the slaughterer is not liable. This is the foundational rule.
The key phrase: 'جاز استحساناً ولا يضمن'.
2
Understand the Basis: Custom
The reason given is that in custom (urf), the owner of the sacrifice does not slaughter himself but delegates to another. Thus, the slaughterer becomes implicitly permitted (ma'dhun dilalah). This is a form of istihsan overriding strict analogy (qiyas) which would require explicit permission.
Custom is a recognized source in Hanafi law.
3
Trace the Analogy (Qiyas)
The text analogizes to the case of a butcher: if a man ties a sheep for slaughter and another person slaughters it without permission, the slaughterer is not liable. The illa (effective cause) is customary delegation.
This analogy is explicit in the source.
4
Distinguish Usurpation and Deposit
If one usurps (ghasb) a goat and sacrifices it, it is valid for his sacrifice because he owns it by prior usurpation. In contrast, if the animal was a deposit (wadi'ah), he becomes liable by slaughter and ownership is not established, so the sacrifice is not valid.
The distinction hinges on ownership transfer: usurpation transfers ownership; deposit does not.
5
Work Through Mixed Animal Cases
Examine the cases from Fatawa Ahiwar: two men's animals mixed, or three with one defective. The judge divides the disputed animal equally but neither sacrifice is valid; the undisputed animal goes to bayt al-mal. For camels/cows, sacrifice is valid for both. Note the differences and reasons.
These cases illustrate how liability and validity are determined when ownership is unclear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنقص من فصار كما لو باع أضحية غيره كان الحكم ما ذكرناه. وذكر في المحيط مطلقاً من غير قيد فقال : ذبح أضحية غيره بلا أمره جاز استحساناً ولا يضمن لأنه في العرف لا يتولى صاحب الأضحية ذبحها بنفسه بل يفوض إلى غيره فصار مأذوناً دلالة كالقصاب إذا شد رجل شاة للذبح فذبحها إنسان بغير أمره لا يضمن ولو باع أضحية واشترى بثمنها غيرها فإن كان الثاني الأول تصدق بالفضل، ولو غصب شاة وضحى بها جاز عن أضحيته لأنه ملكها بالغصب السابق بخلاف ما لو كانت وديعة لأنه يضمنها بالذبح فلم يثبت له الملك إلا بعده. ولو ذبح أضحية غيره بغير أمره عن نفسه، فإن ضمنه المالك قيمتها تجوز عن الذابح دون المالك لأنه ظهر أن الإراقة حصلت على ملكه على ما بينا في المغصوبة، وإن أخذها مذبوحة أجزأت المالك عن التضحية لأنه قد نواها فلا يضره ذبحها غيره على ما بينا. وفي فتاوى أهوار : رجلان ربطاً أضحيتهما في مربط ثم غلطا فتنازعا في واحدة كل منهما مدعيها ولا الأخرى يقضي بالذي تنازعا فيها بينهما نصفين ولا تجوز الأضحية عنهما بهما. وقال يدعي بعضهم : تجوز عنهما جميعاً. والصحيح الأول، والذي لم يتنازعا فيها لبيت المال لأنها مال ضائع، ولو كانت إبلاً وبقراً جازت الأضحية عنهما جميعاً، وإذا ربطوا ثلاثة أضحية في رباط واحد ثم وجدا بواحد عيباً يمنع جواز الأضحية وأنكر كل واحد منهم أن تكون له المعيبة وتنازعوا في الأخريين فالمعيبة لبيت المال لأنها مال ضائع ويقضى بينهم بالأخريين أثلاثاً ا هـ . والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
Less than, so it became as if he sold another's sacrificial animal; the ruling is what we mentioned. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit absolutely without restriction, saying: He slaughtered another's sacrificial animal without his permission; it is permissible by istihsan and he is not liable, because in custom the owner of the sacrifice does not undertake slaughter himself but delegates to another, so he becomes implicitly permitted, like the butcher: if a man ties a sheep for slaughter and another person slaughters it without his permission, he is not liable. And if he sold a sacrificial animal and bought another with its price, then if the second was the first, he gives the surplus in charity. And if he usurped a goat and sacrificed with it, it is valid for his sacrifice because he owned it by prior usurpation, unlike the case of a deposit because he becomes liable by slaughter, so ownership is not established for him except after that. And if he slaughtered another's sacrificial animal without his permission for himself, then if the owner makes him liable for its value, it is valid for the slaughterer not for the owner, because it appears that the shedding of blood occurred on his property as we explained in the case of usurped property. And if he takes it slaughtered, it suffices for the owner for sacrifice because he intended it, so the slaughter by another does not harm him as we explained. And in Fatawa Ahiwar: Two men tied their sacrificial animals in a stable, then they made a mistake and disputed over one, each claiming it and not the other. He judges that what they disputed over is divided equally between them, and the sacrifice is not valid for either of them by them. Some say it is valid for both. The correct is the first. And the one over which they did not dispute goes to the treasury because it is lost property. And if they were camels and cows, the sacrifice is valid for both. And if three people tied three sacrificial animals in one tether, then they found in one a defect that prevents the validity of sacrifice, and each of them denied that the defective one was his, and they disputed over the other two: the defective one goes to the treasury because it is lost property, and judgment is made between them over the other two in thirds. End. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings (ahkam) concerning the sacrifice (udhiyah) of an animal belonging to another person. The text begins by continuing a prior ruling: if someone sells another's sacrificial animal, the ruling is as previously mentioned. Then it cites al-Muhit, stating unconditionally that slaughtering another's animal without permission is valid by istihsan (juridical preference) and the slaughterer is not liable because custom (urf) shows that owners typically delegate slaughter. This is analogous to a butcher who slaughters an animal tied by someone else without explicit permission; he is not liable due to implicit permission (idhn dilalah). The ruling then covers selling a sacrificial animal and buying another with its price: if the second is the first (likely meaning if the purchased animal is the same as the sold one? The text is ambiguous: 'if the second was the first' may refer to a case where the buyer later acquires the original animal? The madhhab's view: give the surplus in charity). Next, if one usurps a goat and sacrifices it, it is valid for his sacrifice because he owns it by prior usurpation (ghasb) — unlike a deposit (wadi'ah), where liability arises from slaughter and ownership is not established. If one slaughters another's animal without permission for himself, and the owner claims its value, the sacrifice is valid for the slaughterer (not the owner) because the blood was shed on his property (since he owns it by virtue of liability). But if the owner takes it slaughtered, it suffices for him because he intended it. Finally, Fatawa Ahiwar presents a case of two men whose animals got mixed: they dispute over one; the judge divides it equally between them, but neither's sacrifice is valid. The undisputed animal goes to bayt al-mal (public treasury). If they were camels or cows, sacrifice is valid for both. For three animals with one defective, the defective goes to bayt al-mal, and the other two are divided in thirds.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference; a method of reasoning that gives a ruling based on equity or custom, overriding strict analogy.
مأذون دلالة (ma'dhun dilalah): Implicit permission inferred from custom (urf) rather than explicit verbal authorization.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; taking another's property wrongfully. In this context, usurpation transfers ownership for the purpose of liability and sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if someone slaughters another's sacrificial animal without permission, what is the ruling by istihsan?
A) It is invalid and the slaughterer must pay compensation.
B) It is valid and the slaughterer is not liable.
C) It is valid only if the owner later approves.
D) It is invalid and the animal is considered carrion.

Key Takeaway
Custom (urf) can grant implicit permission (idhn dilalah), making the sacrifice of another's animal valid without liability, a key application of istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

The Two Types of Makruh: Tahrimi and Tanzihi
Definition and resolution of two types of makruh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition, and apply the classification to practical examples.

Core Idea
Makruh is not monolithic: tahrimi is closer to haram, tanzihi is closer to halal.

The Hanafi school uniquely divides the category of 'makruh' (disliked) into two distinct levels: karahah tahrimiyyah (dislike of prohibition) and karahah tanzihiyyah (dislike of offensiveness). This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes this distinction by first noting an earlier disagreement among the founding Imams—Imam Muhammad considered every makruh as essentially haram, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf held it is 'closer to haram'. The author resolves this by explaining that the definition of 'closer to haram' applies only to makruh tahrimi, while the other type, makruh tanzihi, is closer to halal. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly weighing evidence in fatwa and practice.

Guided Path
1
1. Grasp the linguistic and technical meaning
Start with the Arabic term karahah: it is the opposite of love and satisfaction, but not the opposite of will (irada). The Shariah meaning builds on this: what the Lawgiver dislikes without a definitively prohibiting text.
The linguistic note helps you see that 'dislike' does not imply absence of divine will—Allah wills disbelief but does not love it.
2
2. Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad held that every makruh is in reality haram, but the label 'haram' is withheld because the evidence is not qat'i (definitive). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said it is merely 'closer to haram'. Compare this to the wajib/fard distinction.
This is the base of the ikhtilaf that the author will resolve.
3
3. See how the author resolves the dispute
The author declares that the definition of 'closer to haram' applies specifically to makruh tahrimi (dislike of prohibition). Makruh tanzihi (dislike of offensiveness) is defined as 'closer to halal'. Thus the two types become distinct rulings with different consequences.
This resolution became the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the school.
4
4. Apply the classification to examples
Test the definition: on the nights of sacrifice, slaughter is makruh tanzihi (closer to halal) because omitting it is not sinful. But selling the sacrificial animal's milk or wool is makruh tahrimi (closer to haram) because it involves misuse of the sacrifice, based on a non-definitive text.
The passage mentions these examples; identify which type each one falls under.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
المكروه إلى الحرام أقرب.
أورد كتاب الكراهية بعد الأضحية لأن عامة مسائل كل واحد منهما لم يخل من أصل أو فرع يرد فيه الكراهة، ألا ترى أن الأضحية في ليالي أيام النحر مكروهة، وكذا في التصرف في الأضحية يجز صوفها وحلب لبنها، وكذا ذبح الكتابي وغير ذلك كما أن الأمر في كتاب الكراهية لذلك. وترجم المؤلف بالكراهية لأن بيان المكروه أهم من غيره لوجوب الاحتراز عنه. وترجم محمد في الأصل بالاستحسان لما فيه مما استحسنه الشارع وقبحه. وترجم القدوري في مختصره بالحظر والإباحة لما فيه مما عنه منع الشرع وأباحه. والكراهية مصدر كره الشيء كرها وكراهة وكراهية. قال في الميزان: هي ضد المحبة والرضا، قال الله تعالى: {وعسى أن تكرهوا شيئاً وهو خير لكم} [البقرة: 216] الخ. فالمكروه خلاف المندوب والمحبوب لغة وليس بضد الإرادة كما توهمه الشارح وجعل الكراهة ضد الإرادة بل هو كما تقدم في الميزان، لأن الله تعالى يريد الكفر والمعاصي ولا يحبهما كما قرر في علم الكلام. وهي في الشريعة ما سيذكره المؤلف. قال رحمه الله: (المكروه إلى الحرام أقرب) ونص محمد أن كل مكروه حرام وإنما لم يطلق عليه لفظ الحرام لأنه لم يجد فيه نصاً قطعياً، فكان نسبة المكروه إلى الحرام عند محمد كنسبة الواجب إلى الفرض. وعن الإمام وأبي يوسف أنه إلى الحرام أقرب، وهذا الحد للمكروه كراهة تحريم، وأما المكروه كراهة تنزيه فإلى الحلال أقرب؛ هذا خلاصة ما ذكروه في الكتب المعتبرة. ولبعض المتأخرين كلمات هنا طويلة الذيل لا حاصل لها تركناها عمداً.
Chapter of Disliked Actions. The disliked is closer to the prohibited. The author included the chapter of Karahiyah after the chapter of Sacrifice because generally the issues of each of them are not free from an origin or branch in which dislike occurs; do you not see that the sacrifice on the nights of the days of Nahr is disliked, and similarly in disposing of the sacrifice by shearing its wool and milking its milk, and similarly the slaughter by a Kitabi, and other things, just as the matter in the chapter of Karahiyah is for that. The author entitled it 'Karahiyah' because explaining the disliked is more important than other things due to the obligation of avoiding it. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) entitled his book 'al-Istihsan' because of what it contains that the Lawgiver deemed good or bad. Al-Quduri titled his abridgment 'al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah' because of what it contains that the law has prohibited or permitted. Karahiyah is the verbal noun of hating something with hate, hatred, and dislike. It is said in al-Mizan: it is the opposite of love and satisfaction; Allah says: 'But it may be that you dislike something while it is good for you' [Quran 2:216] etc. So linguistically, al-makruh is the opposite of al-mandub (recommended) and al-mahbub (beloved), and it is not the opposite of al-iradah (will) as the commentator imagined, making karahah the opposite of iradah. Rather it is as previously mentioned in al-Mizan, because Allah wills disbelief and sins but does not love them, as established in theology. In the Shariah, it is what the author will mention. The author said: (The disliked is closer to the prohibited). And Muhammad stated that every disliked thing is prohibited, but the word 'haram' is not applied to it because he did not find a definitive text for it. So the relation of the disliked to the prohibited according to Muhammad is like the relation of the wajib to the fard. And from Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is closer to the prohibited. This definition is for the disliked with the karahah of tahrim (dislike of prohibition). As for the disliked with karahah tanzih (dislike of offensiveness), it is closer to the permissible. This is the summary of what they mentioned in the reliable books. And some later scholars have lengthy words here, which we deliberately left out.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the opening statement of the chapter on Karahiyah. The author first explains why this chapter follows the chapter of Udhiyah (sacrifice): many issues in sacrifice involve dislike. He then notes that different Hanafi authors titled their works differently (Karahiyah, Istihsan, Hazr wa Ibahah) reflecting the content. The main focus is defining makruh. Linguistically, karahah is the opposite of love. In Shariah, Imam Muhammad held that every makruh is actually haram but not labeled as such due to lack of qat'i (definitive) textual evidence, analogous to wajib being considered fard but not called fard. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf held that makruh (in the sense of karahah tahrimi) is closer to haram, not absolutely haram. The author clarifies that this definition of 'makruh closer to haram' applies specifically to karahah tahrimi (dislike of prohibition), which is the stronger type. The weaker type, karahah tanzihi (dislike of offensiveness), is closer to halal (permissible). This is the standard Hanafi framework: makruh tahrimi is a prohibited act with non-definitive evidence, while makruh tanzihi is a disliked but not prohibited act.

Key Terms
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): Dislike of prohibition: an act that is closer to haram, based on non-definitive evidence; omission is rewarded, commission does not incur punishment but is blameworthy.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): Dislike of offensiveness: an act closer to halal; omission is rewarded, commission is not sinful but is less virtuous.
المكروه (al-makruh): Linguistically, the opposite of beloved; in Shariah, it is what the Lawgiver dislikes but not with a definitive prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between karahah tahrimi and karahah tanzihi?
A) Karahah tahrimi is closer to halal, while karahah tanzihi is closer to haram.
B) Karahah tahrimi is closer to haram, while karahah tanzihi is closer to halal.
C) Both are equally close to haram.
D) Karahah tahrimi is a sin, while karahah tanzihi is not.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves an internal dispute by dividing makruh into tahrimi (near-prohibition) and tanzihi (mere offensiveness), each with distinct legal consequences.

Hanafi Doctrine of Iman: Definition, Increase, and the Muqallid
Defining iman and its characteristics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of iman, explain why it does not increase or decrease, and identify the conditions for the faith of a muqallid (imitator).

Core Idea
Iman is affirmation by heart and tongue, not actions; it neither increases nor decreases.

This lesson explores the foundational Hanafi creed on iman as presented in al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah. The passage defines iman, addresses the classic debate on whether it can increase or decrease, and discusses the validity of the faith of a person who believes without proof.

Guided Path
1
Define iman according to the Hanafi school
Locate the definition in the text: 'الإيمان هو الإقرار باللسان والاعتقاد بالجنان'. Note that affirmation by tongue is a condition for the able.
2
Explain the Hanafi stance on increase/decrease
The text explicitly states 'الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص' because iman is not from actions. Contrast with the Shafi’i view.
3
Analyze the dispute between Bukhara and Samarkand scholars
The text records a dispute on whether iman is created or uncreated. Understand the resolution: guidance is uncreated, the act of faith is created.
4
Determine the ruling for the muqallid (imitator)
Read the cases from Jami' al-Jawami' and al-Nawazil: a person who believes the pillars but cannot articulate may still be a believer if he has basic knowledge.
Focus on the practical judgment: presenting Islam to those who cannot answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في الفتاوى السراجية في هذا الكتاب باباً في مسائل الاعتقاديات وقدمه وهو أولى بالذكر والتقديم قال : الإيمان هو الإقرار باللسان والاعتقاد بالجنان [؟] وذلك أن يقرّوا بوحدانية الله تعالى وصفاته الأزلية وبجميع ما جاء من عنده من كتب ويعتقد بقلبه ذلك. والإقرار باللسان شرط في حق القادر على النطق على ظاهر الجواب. وقيل: الإيمان هو الاعتقاد بالقلب. والإيمان بالتفاصيل ليس بواجب بل إذا آمن بالجملة كفي. والإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص لأن الإيمان عندنا ليس من الأعمال. إيمان اليائس غير مقبول وتوبة اليائس مقبولة. الإيمان غير مخلوق عند أئمة بخارى وعند أئمة سمرقند مخلوق، وقيل لا خلاف بينهم في الحقيقة لأن أئمة بخارى قالوا الإيمان هداية الرب لعبده إلى معرفته وذلك غير مخلوق، وأئمة سمرقند قالوا الإيمان فعل العبد وأنه مخلوق، وعن هذا تعرف جواب من أن الإيمان عطائي أو كسبي. إيمان المقلد وهو الذي اعتقد أركان الإسلام بلا دليل. وفي جامع الجوامع قال أبو القاسم: من تعلم في الصغر آمنت بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر والقدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى وتعلم أنه إيمان لكن لا يحسن تعبيره لا يحكم بإسلامه. وقال أبو الليث: إن سأل فارسياً فقال هذا عرفت [؟] يحكم بإسلامه. قال: وإن يعرض عليه الإسلام [؟]. وفي النوازل قال الفقيه: إذا كان الرجل لا يحسن العبارة ولا يحل [؟] لو سئل بالفارسية يعرف أن الله واحد وأن الأنبياء رسل الله عز وجل وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيها وأن الله يبعث من في القبور ويقول كنت عرفت أن الأمر هكذا كان هذا مؤمناً، وإن كان لا عنه [؟] وإذا سئل عن هذا قال لا أعلم بذلك فلا دين له ويعرض عليه الإسلام، فإن أسلم وكانت له امرأة يجدد نكاحها. وفي السراجية: المؤمن لا يخرج عن الإيمان بارتكاب الكبيرة، وإذا مات بغير توبة فهو في مشيئة الله تعالى إن شاء غفر له وإن شاء عذبه بقدر جنايته أو أقل ثم يدخله الجنة. والقرآن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق ولا محدث، والمكتوب في المصاحف دال على كلام الله تعالى وأنه مخلوق. رؤية الله تعالى في الآخرة حق يراه أهل الجنة في الآخرة بلا كيفية ولا تشبيه ولا محازاة، أما رؤية الله تعالى في المنام أكثرهم قالوا لا تجوز والسكوت في هذا الباب أحوط. القدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى بمشيئته وإرادته القديمة إلا أن المعاصي ليست برضا الله تعالى. وفي الحاوي وعن أبي سلمة الفقيه أنه قال: هذه عشرة مسائل التي وجدت عليها السلف أهل الهداية والجماعة من آمن بها كان منهم، ومن لم يؤمن بها فهو من مشايخ [؟] صاحب هوى وبدعة. ثم عد هذه العشرة وقال قال شيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن القاضي: إن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد وأفعالهم بقضاء الله تعالى ومشيئته، وأن الله تعالى خالق لم يزل، وأن الله تعالى له علم موصوف في الأزل، وأن الله تعالى يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد إذا كان أصلح للعباد أو لم يكن لا يسأل عما يفعل وهم يسألون، وأن شفاعة محمد حق لأهل الكبائر من أمته وأن عذاب القبر حق، وأنه يرجى من الله تعالى أن يعطي العباد ما يسألونه من دعائهم. وفي السراجية صفات الله تعالى قديمة كلها من غير تفصيل بين صفات الذات وصفات الفعل وأنها قائمة بذات الله تعالى لا هو ولا غيره كالواحد من العشرة، والله تعالى ليس بجسم ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا حال بمكان، ثم إن الله تعالى...
And he mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah in this book a chapter on creedal matters and placed it first, and it is more deserving of mention and precedence. He said: Faith (iman) is affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart, such that they affirm the oneness of Allah Most High and His eternal attributes, and all what came from Him of books, and believe in his heart that. Affirmation by the tongue is a condition for the one able to speak, according to the apparent answer. And it was said: Faith is belief in the heart. Believing in details is not obligatory; rather if one believes in general, it suffices. Faith does not increase nor decrease, because in our view faith is not from actions. The faith of the desperate person is not accepted, but his repentance is accepted. Faith is uncreated according to the imams of Bukhara, and according to the imams of Samarkand it is created, and it is said there is no dispute between them in reality because the imams of Bukhara said faith is the guidance of the Lord to His servant to know Him, and that is uncreated, and the imams of Samarkand said faith is the act of the servant and that it is created, and from this you know the answer to whether faith is gratuitous or acquired. The faith of the imitator (muqallid) is one who believes the pillars of Islam without proof. And in Jami' al-Jawami', Abu al-Qasim said: Whoever learns in childhood 'I believe in Allah and His angels and His books and His messengers and the Last Day and destiny, its good and evil from Allah Most High' and learns that it is faith, but he cannot express it well, he is not judged to be a Muslim. And Abu al-Layth said: If he asks a Persian and says 'I have known this' [؟], he is judged to be a Muslim. He said: And if Islam is presented to him [؟]. And in al-Nawazil, al-Faqih said: If a man cannot express well and it is not permissible [؟] if asked in Persian, he knows that Allah is one and the prophets are messengers of Allah and that the Hour is coming without doubt and Allah will resurrect those in the graves, and he says 'I knew the matter was thus', this one is a believer. And if he cannot [؟] and when asked about this he says 'I do not know that', then he has no religion and Islam is presented to him; if he accepts Islam and he has a wife, he renews her marriage. And in al-Sirajiyyah: The believer does not leave faith by committing a major sin, and if he dies without repentance, he is under the will of Allah; if He wills He forgives him, if He wills He punishes him according to his crime or less, then enters him into Paradise. And the Qur'an is the speech of Allah Most High, uncreated and not temporal; what is written in the mus'hafs indicates the speech of Allah and that it is created. Seeing Allah in the Hereafter is true; the people of Paradise will see Him in the Hereafter without modality, without anthropomorphism, and without direction. As for seeing Allah in a dream, most of them said it is not allowed, and silence on this matter is more cautious. Destiny, its good and evil, is from Allah Most High by His eternal will and desire, except that sins are not with the pleasure of Allah Most High. And in al-Hawi, from Abu Salama al-Faqih that he said: These are ten issues upon which the pious predecessors, the people of guidance and the community, are found; whoever believes in them is of them, and whoever does not believe in them is from the shaykhs [؟] of the people of desire and innovation. Then he counted these ten and said: The shaykh, Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Qadi, said: Indeed Allah Most High created the actions of the servants, and their actions are by the decree of Allah and His will; and indeed Allah Most High is the Creator, eternal; and indeed Allah Most High has knowledge described in eternity; and indeed Allah Most High does what He wills and judges what He wills, whether it is better for the servants or not; He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked; and indeed the intercession of Muhammad (peace be upon him) is true for the people of major sins from his community; and indeed the punishment of the grave is true; and it is hoped from Allah Most High that He will give the servants what they ask of Him through their supplications. And in al-Sirajiyyah: All the attributes of Allah Most High are eternal, without distinction between attributes of essence and attributes of action, and they subsist in the essence of Allah, neither He nor other [؟] like the one from ten; and Allah Most High is not a body, nor a substance, nor an accident, nor a located state; then Allah Most High...
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a collection of creedal statements from various early Hanafi sources, primarily al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah. The author has placed this chapter on creedal matters at the beginning of the book on Karahiyah. The first part defines iman (faith) as affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart, with a discussion of whether detailed belief is required. It notes the classical Hanafi position that iman does not increase or decrease, rejecting the Mutazilite view that iman includes actions. There is a debate between the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand on whether iman is created or uncreated, which is resolved by distinguishing between the act of guidance (uncreated) and the act of the servant (created). Then it addresses the case of a muqallid (one who believes without proof) and the judgment of those who cannot articulate their faith properly. Important rulings: a person who believes but cannot express may still be a believer; a person who cannot answer basic creedal questions must be taught Islam. The creed also affirms that major sins do not expel a believer from faith (contra the Kharijites), and that such sinners are under God's will. The Qur'an is uncreated speech of Allah, but the physical mus'haf is created. Seeing Allah in the afterlife is true; seeing in a dream is controversial. Destiny, good and evil, is from Allah, but sins are not pleasing to Him. Ten issues from the Salaf are listed, covering divine creation of actions, eternal knowledge, freedom of divine will, intercession, punishment of the grave, and answer to supplications. Finally, attributes of Allah are eternal and not differentiated; Allah is not a body, substance, accident, or located. This passage represents the standard Maturidi-Hanafi aqidah.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-iman): Affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart; it does not include actions and does not increase or decrease.
إيمان المقلد (iman al-muqallid): The faith of the one who believes the pillars of Islam without proof is considered valid if he believes correctly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does iman not increase or decrease?
A) Because it is a matter of belief only, not including actions.
B) Because it is created and therefore fixed.
C) Because the text says so without reason.
D) Because actions cannot affect the heart.

Key Takeaway
Iman is stable affirmation of heart and tongue; it does not change with actions, and the muqallid's simple belief is valid.

intermediate
12 min
Major Sins, Intercession, Qur'an, Ru'yah, and Qadar
Creedal rulings on sin, intercession, Qur'an, ru'yah, qadar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on major sins not removing faith, intercession for sinners, the uncreatedness of the Qur'an, seeing Allah in the hereafter, and the decree of good and evil.

Core Idea
A believer does not leave faith by major sins; intercession is for sinners; Qur'an is uncreated; ru'yah is true; qadar is from Allah.

This lesson covers several foundational Hanafi creedal points from al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah: the status of major sinners, intercession of the Prophet, the nature of the Qur'an, vision of Allah, and divine destiny. These represent core Maturidi-Hanafi beliefs that distinguish them from other sects.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on major sins
Read: 'المؤمن لا يخرج عن الإيمان بارتكاب الكبيرة'. Note that the sinner remains under Allah's will.
2
Affirm intercession for major sinners
The text states intercession is true for the people of major sins from the Ummah.
3
Differentiate between Qur'an and mushaf
The Qur'an is uncreated speech; the written mushaf is created and indicates the speech.
4
State the belief in ru'yah (seeing Allah)
The people of Paradise will see Allah in the Hereafter without modality or direction. Seeing in a dream is rejected by most.
5
Explain qadar (divine decree)
All good and evil occur by Allah's will, but sins are not with His pleasure.

الأزلية وبجميع ما جاء من عنده من كتب ويعتقد بقلبه ذلك. والإقرار باللسان شرط في حق القادر على النطق على ظاهر الجواب. وقيل: الإيمان هو الاعتقاد بالقلب. والإيمان بالتفاصيل ليس بواجب بل إذا آمن بالجملة كفي. والإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص لأن الإيمان عندنا ليس من الأعمال. إيمان اليائس غير مقبول وتوبة اليائس مقبولة. الإيمان غير مخلوق عند أئمة بخارى وعند أئمة سمرقند مخلوق، وقيل لا خلاف بينهم في الحقيقة لأن أئمة بخارى قالوا الإيمان هداية الرب لعبده إلى معرفته وذلك غير مخلوق، وأئمة سمرقند قالوا الإيمان فعل العبد وأنه مخلوق، وعن هذا تعرف جواب من أن الإيمان عطائي أو كسبي. إيمان المقلد وهو الذي اعتقد أركان The Ten Salaf Principles and Divine Attributes
Listing the ten Salaf issues and divine attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten creedal principles transmitted from the Salaf as mentioned in al-Hawi, and explain the Hanafi doctrine on divine attributes and transcendence.

Core Idea
The ten principles affirm divine creation of actions, eternal knowledge, intercession, grave punishment, and Allah's transcendence beyond body and substance.

This lesson presents ten issues that the early generations (Salaf) agreed upon, as narrated by Abu Salama al-Faqih in al-Hawi. It also covers the Hanafi-Maturidi stance on divine attributes being eternal and subsisting in Allah's essence, and the negation of corporeality.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the ten issues from the passage
The text lists ten points: creation of actions, divine eternal knowledge, divine will, intercession, grave punishment, etc. Identify each.
The text does not list them sequentially; identify from the quote.
2
Understand the Hanafi view on attributes
Attributes are eternal, subsisting in the essence, without distinction between essential and active attributes.
3
Affirm transcendence (tanzih)
Allah is not a body, substance, accident, nor located in a place.

Source Text

كفي. والإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص لأن الإيمان عندنا ليس من الأعمال. إيمان اليائس غير مقبول وتوبة اليائس مقبولة. الإيمان غير مخلوق عند أئمة بخارى وعند أئمة سمرقند مخلوق، وقيل لا خلاف بينهم في الحقيقة لأن أئمة بخارى قالوا الإيمان هداية الرب لعبده إلى معرفته وذلك غير مخلوق، وأئمة سمرقند قالوا الإيمان فعل العبد وأنه مخلوق، وعن هذا تعرف جواب من أن الإيمان عطائي أو كسبي. إيمان المقلد وهو الذي اعتقد أركان الإسلام بلا دليل. وفي جامع الجوامع قال أبو القاسم: من تعلم في الصغر آمنت بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر والقدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى وتعلم أنه إيمان لكن لا يحسن تعبيره لا يحكم بإسلامه. وقال أبو الليث: إن سأل فارسياً فقال هذا عرفت [؟] يحكم بإسلامه. قال: وإن يعرض عليه الإسلام [؟]. وفي النوازل قال الفقيه: إذا كان الرجل لا يحسن العبارة ولا يحل [؟] لو سئل بالفارسية يعرف أن الله واحد وأن الأنبياء رسل الله عز وجل وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيها وأن الله يبعث من في القبور ويقول كنت عرفت أن الأمر هكذا كان هذا مؤمناً، وإن كان لا عنه [؟] وإذا سئل عن هذا قال لا أعلم بذلك فلا دين له ويعرض عليه الإسلام، فإن أسلم وكانت له امرأة يجدد نكاحها. وفي السراجية: المؤمن لا يخرج عن الإيمان بارتكاب الكبيرة، وإذا مات بغير توبة فهو في مشيئة الله تعالى إن شاء غفر له وإن شاء عذبه بقدر جنايته أو أقل ثم يدخله الجنة. والقرآن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق ولا محدث، والمكتوب في المصاحف دال على كلام الله تعالى وأنه مخلوق. رؤية الله تعالى في الآخرة حق يراه أهل الجنة في الآخرة بلا كيفية ولا تشبيه ولا محازاة، أما رؤية الله تعالى في المنام أكثرهم قالوا لا تجوز والسكوت في هذا الباب أحوط. القدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى بمشيئته وإرادته القديمة إلا أن المعاصي ليست برضا الله تعالى. وفي الحاوي وعن أبي سلمة الفقيه أنه قال: هذه عشرة مسائل التي وجدت عليها السلف أهل الهداية والجماعة من آمن بها كان منهم، ومن لم يؤمن بها فهو من مشايخ [؟] صاحب هوى وبدعة. ثم عد هذه العشرة وقال قال شيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن القاضي: إن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد وأفعالهم بقضاء الله تعالى ومشيئته، وأن الله تعالى خالق لم يزل، وأن الله تعالى له علم موصوف في الأزل، وأن الله تعالى يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد إذا كان أصلح للعباد أو لم يكن لا يسأل عما يفعل وهم يسألون، وأن شفاعة محمد حق لأهل الكبائر من أمته وأن عذاب القبر حق، وأنه يرجى من الله تعالى أن يعطي العباد ما يسألونه من دعائهم. وفي السراجية صفات الله تعالى قديمة كلها من غير تفصيل بين صفات الذات وصفات الفعل وأنها قائمة بذات الله تعالى لا هو ولا غيره كالواحد من العشرة، والله تعالى ليس بجسم ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا حال بمكان، ثم إن الله تعالى...
And he mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah in this book a chapter on creedal matters and placed it first, and it is more deserving of mention and precedence. He said: Faith (iman) is affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart, such that they affirm the oneness of Allah Most High and His eternal attributes, and all what came from Him of books, and believe in his heart that. Affirmation by the tongue is a condition for the one able to speak, according to the apparent answer. And it was said: Faith is belief in the heart. Believing in details is not obligatory; rather if one believes in general, it suffices. Faith does not increase nor decrease, because in our view faith is not from actions. The faith of the desperate person is not accepted, but his repentance is accepted. Faith is uncreated according to the imams of Bukhara, and according to the imams of Samarkand it is created, and it is said there is no dispute between them in reality because the imams of Bukhara said faith is the guidance of the Lord to His servant to know Him, and that is uncreated, and the imams of Samarkand said faith is the act of the servant and that it is created, and from this you know the answer to whether faith is gratuitous or acquired. The faith of the imitator (muqallid) is one who believes the pillars of Islam without proof. And in Jami' al-Jawami', Abu al-Qasim said: Whoever learns in childhood 'I believe in Allah and His angels and His books and His messengers and the Last Day and destiny, its good and evil from Allah Most High' and learns that it is faith, but he cannot express it well, he is not judged to be a Muslim. And Abu al-Layth said: If he asks a Persian and says 'I have known this' [؟], he is judged to be a Muslim. He said: And if Islam is presented to him [؟]. And in al-Nawazil, al-Faqih said: If a man cannot express well and it is not permissible [؟] if asked in Persian, he knows that Allah is one and the prophets are messengers of Allah and that the Hour is coming without doubt and Allah will resurrect those in the graves, and he says 'I knew the matter was thus', this one is a believer. And if he cannot [؟] and when asked about this he says 'I do not know that', then he has no religion and Islam is presented to him; if he accepts Islam and he has a wife, he renews her marriage. And in al-Sirajiyyah: The believer does not leave faith by committing a major sin, and if he dies without repentance, he is under the will of Allah; if He wills He forgives him, if He wills He punishes him according to his crime or less, then enters him into Paradise. And the Qur'an is the speech of Allah Most High, uncreated and not temporal; what is written in the mus'hafs indicates the speech of Allah and that it is created. Seeing Allah in the Hereafter is true; the people of Paradise will see Him in the Hereafter without modality, without anthropomorphism, and without direction. As for seeing Allah in a dream, most of them said it is not allowed, and silence on this matter is more cautious. Destiny, its good and evil, is from Allah Most High by His eternal will and desire, except that sins are not with the pleasure of Allah Most High. And in al-Hawi, from Abu Salama al-Faqih that he said: These are ten issues upon which the pious predecessors, the people of guidance and the community, are found; whoever believes in them is of them, and whoever does not believe in them is from the shaykhs [؟] of the people of desire and innovation. Then he counted these ten and said: The shaykh, Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Qadi, said: Indeed Allah Most High created the actions of the servants, and their actions are by the decree of Allah and His will; and indeed Allah Most High is the Creator, eternal; and indeed Allah Most High has knowledge described in eternity; and indeed Allah Most High does what He wills and judges what He wills, whether it is better for the servants or not; He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked; and indeed the intercession of Muhammad (peace be upon him) is true for the people of major sins from his community; and indeed the punishment of the grave is true; and it is hoped from Allah Most High that He will give the servants what they ask of Him through their supplications. And in al-Sirajiyyah: All the attributes of Allah Most High are eternal, without distinction between attributes of essence and attributes of action, and they subsist in the essence of Allah, neither He nor other [؟] like the one from ten; and Allah Most High is not a body, nor a substance, nor an accident, nor a located state; then Allah Most High...
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a collection of creedal statements from various early Hanafi sources, primarily al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah. The author has placed this chapter on creedal matters at the beginning of the book on Karahiyah. The first part defines iman (faith) as affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart, with a discussion of whether detailed belief is required. It notes the classical Hanafi position that iman does not increase or decrease, rejecting the Mutazilite view that iman includes actions. There is a debate between the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand on whether iman is created or uncreated, which is resolved by distinguishing between the act of guidance (uncreated) and the act of the servant (created). Then it addresses the case of a muqallid (one who believes without proof) and the judgment of those who cannot articulate their faith properly. Important rulings: a person who believes but cannot express may still be a believer; a person who cannot answer basic creedal questions must be taught Islam. The creed also affirms that major sins do not expel a believer from faith (contra the Kharijites), and that such sinners are under God's will. The Qur'an is uncreated speech of Allah, but the physical mus'haf is created. Seeing Allah in the afterlife is true; seeing in a dream is controversial. Destiny, good and evil, is from Allah, but sins are not pleasing to Him. Ten issues from the Salaf are listed, covering divine creation of actions, eternal knowledge, freedom of divine will, intercession, punishment of the grave, and answer to supplications. Finally, attributes of Allah are eternal and not differentiated; Allah is not a body, substance, accident, or located. This passage represents the standard Maturidi-Hanafi aqidah.

Key Terms
صفات الله تعالى (sifat Allah ta'ala): The attributes of Allah, all eternal, subsisting in His essence, without distinction between essential and active.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how are the attributes of Allah described?
A) Some are eternal, some are created in time.
B) All are eternal and subsist in His essence.
C) They are separate from His essence.
D) They are not real but metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The ten Salaf issues form the core of Hanafi creed, and divine attributes are all eternal with Allah's transcendence affirmed.

Definition and Minimum Requirements of Iman
Defines Iman, its increase/decrease, and the minimum belief for a Muslim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum requirement of Iman according to the Hanafi school and explain why Iman does not increase or decrease.

Core Idea
Iman is heart affirmation; detailed belief not obligatory – summary suffices for salvation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the foundational Hanafi understanding of Iman. It clarifies that a person does not need to know every detail of the creed; believing in the essentials in one's heart is sufficient. The passage also addresses controversial points: whether Iman increases or decreases, whether it is created or uncreated, and the validity of a muqallid's faith. These rulings have practical implications for who is considered a Muslim in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on detailed belief
The author states that detailed belief (iman bil-tafasil) is not obligatory. Instead, summary belief (iman bil-jumla) suffices. Locate this statement and note the ruling.
This is a facilitative ruling of the Hanafi school, easing entry into Islam.
2
Analyze the nature of Iman: no increase or decrease
The text asserts that Iman neither increases nor decreases because Iman is not from actions. Understand the Hanafi position that Iman is tasdiq bi al-qalb, a constant affirmation, and that actions are separate.
This contrasts with the Ash'ari view that Iman increases with obedience and decreases with sin.
3
Examine the Iman of the muqallid
The author defines the muqallid as one who believes the pillars of Islam without evidence. Note that the Hanafi school validates such faith, unlike the Mu'tazila.
This ruling is based on the principle that tasdiq is the essence of Iman, not rational proof.
4
Consider practical cases of inability to articulate
The passage gives a ruling on a person who cannot articulate the creed well but knows it in his heart. If he affirms when asked in a language he understands, he is a Muslim. If he cannot affirm, he is a disbeliever.
This shows that the core requirement is knowledge and affirmation, not eloquence.
5
Apply the ruling on marriage renewal
The passage ends with a note: if a non-Muslim embraces Islam after his marriage was invalid, the marriage must be renewed. This connects Iman to contractual validity.
This is a practical consequence of the person's previous non-Muslim status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
الاعتقاد بالقلب والإيمان بالتفاصيل ليس بواجب بل إذا آمن بالجملة كفي. والإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص لأن الإيمان عندنا ليس من الأعمال إيمان اليائس غير مقبول وتوبة اليائس مقبولة، الإيمان غير مخلوق عند أئمة بخارى وعند أئمة سمرقند مخلوق، وقيل لا خلاف بينهم في الحقيقة لأن أئمة بخارى قالوا الإيمان هداية الرب لعبده إلى معرفته وذلك غير مخلوق، وأئمة سمرقند قالوا الإيمان فعل العبد وأنه مخلوق، وعن هذا تعرف جواب من أن الإيمان عطائي أو كسبي. أيمان المقلد وهو الذي اعتقد أركان الإسلام بلا دليل. وفي جامع الجوامع قال أبو القاسم : من تعلم في الصغر آمنت بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر والقدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى وتعلم أنه إيمان لكن لا يحسن تعبره لا يحكم بإسلامه. وقال أبو الليث : إن سأل فارسياً فقال هذا عرفت يحكم بإسلامه قال : وإن يعرض عليه الإسلام وفي النوازل قال الفقيه : إذا كان الرجل لا يحسن العبارة ولا يحل لو سئل بالفارسية يعرف أن الله واحد وأن الأنبياء رسل الله عز وجل وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيها وأن الله يبعث من في القبور ويقول كنت عرفت أن الأمر هكذا كان هذا مؤمناً، وإن كان لا عنه وإذا سئل عن هذا قال لا أعلم بذلك فلا دين له ويعرض عليه الإسلام، فإن أسلم وكانت له امرأة يجدد نكاحها
Book of Disliked Matters. Belief with the heart and detailed faith is not obligatory; rather, if he believes in summary it suffices. Iman does not increase nor decrease because Iman, according to us, is not from actions. The Iman of the despairing person is not accepted, but his repentance is accepted. Iman is uncreated according to the imams of Bukhara, and according to the imams of Samarkand it is created. It is said there is no real difference between them because the imams of Bukhara said Iman is the guidance of the Lord to His servant to know Him, and that is uncreated; the imams of Samarkand said Iman is an act of the servant and it is created. From this you know the answer to whether Iman is a gift or acquired. The Iman of the muqallid is one who believes the pillars of Islam without evidence. And in Jami' al-Jawami', Abu al-Qasim said: One who learned in childhood 'I believe in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and destiny its good and evil from Allah' and learned that it is Iman, but cannot express it well, his Islam is not judged. Abu al-Layth said: If a Persian is asked and says 'This I know,' he is judged a Muslim. He said: If he is presented with Islam. And in al-Nawazil, al-Faqih said: If a man cannot express well, and it is not permissible, if asked in Persian he knows that Allah is One, the prophets are messengers of Allah, the Hour is coming without doubt, Allah will resurrect those in the graves, and says 'I knew the matter is so,' he is a believer. If he cannot, and when asked about this he says 'I do not know that,' then he has no religion and Islam is presented to him. If he embraces Islam and has a wife, his marriage is renewed.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage defines the Hanafi position on the nature and minimum requirements of Iman. The author begins by stating that detailed creedal belief (iman bil-tafasil) is not obligatory; rather, summary belief (iman bil-jumla) suffices for being a Muslim. This is a ruling from the Hanafi school that facilitates entry into Islam. Iman, according to Abu Hanifa, is affirmation in the heart (tasdiq bi al-qalb) and is not increased by actions or decreased by sins; thus it remains constant. The Iman of a person in despair (yā'is) of salvation is not accepted, though his repentance is accepted. Then the text discusses the theological debate on whether Iman is created (makhluq) or uncreated (ghayr makhluq). The imams of Bukhara considered Iman as divine guidance, which is uncreated; the imams of Samarkand considered it an act of the servant, hence created. The author reconciles this as a semantic difference. The 'Iman of the muqallid' refers to one who believes the pillars of Islam without evidence; such Iman is valid. A crucial discussion follows: a person who believed the fundamentals in childhood but cannot articulate them properly is still judged a Muslim if he knows them when asked in a language he understands, as per Abu al-Layth. However, if he cannot affirm them at all, he is considered a disbeliever and must be invited to Islam. If he accepts Islam, his previous marriage contract must be renewed because it was invalid while he was a non-Muslim.

Key Terms
الإيمان بالتفاصيل (al-iman bi al-tafasil): Detailed belief in each article of faith as specified in the creeds.
أيمان المقلد (iman al-muqallid): The faith of one who accepts the basics of Islam without knowing the evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the minimum requirement for a person to be considered a Muslim regarding belief?
A) Belief in all detailed articles of faith with evidence
B) Summary belief in the heart, even if unable to articulate it
C) Daily recitation of the Shahada
D) Performing the five pillars

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the minimum for Iman is summary belief in the six articles affirmed in the heart; detailed knowledge is not obligatory, and the faith of a muqallid is valid.
