The Ten Doctrines of Ahl al-Sunnah
Creedal rulings of Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten foundational doctrines of Ahl al-Sunnah as enumerated by Abu Salama al-Faqih and explain the Hanafi position on each.

Core Idea
The grave sinner remains a believer; the Quran is uncreated; ru'yah is true; qadr includes good and evil but Allah does not approve of sin.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents core Hanafi creedal positions that distinguish Ahl al-Sunnah from Khawarij, Mu'tazila, and other sects. The text lists four major topics: the grave sinner, the Quran, seeing Allah (ru'yah), and destiny (qadr), followed by a comprehensive list of ten principles compiled by Abu Salama al-Faqih. Understanding these doctrines is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh, as they form the theological foundation upon which many legal rulings rest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four main topics
The passage divides into two parts: the first discusses four major creedal issues (grave sinner, Quran, ru'yah, qadr) in detail; the second lists ten specific principles from Abu Salama al-Faqih. Read carefully to separate these.
2
Extract the Hanafi position on the grave sinner
Note the key points: the believer does not leave faith by committing a major sin; after death without repentance, he is under Allah's will—He may forgive or punish, but eventually enters Paradise.
This opposes the Khawarij who declare such a person a kafir, and the Mu'tazila who place him in a middle state.
3
Extract the Hanafi position on the Quran and ru'yah
The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah; the mus'haf is a created indicator. Ru'yah in the Hereafter is true without modality; seeing Allah in dreams is generally impermissible, and silence is recommended.
The Mu'tazila hold the Quran is created and deny ru'yah.
4
Extract the Hanafi position on qadr
Both good and evil are from Allah's eternal will, but sins are not with His pleasure. This affirms divine decree while upholding that Allah does not approve of evil.
This balances predestination and moral responsibility.
5
Memorize the ten principles of Ahl al-Sunnah
From the second part, list the ten principles: Allah creates actions, actions are by His decree, Allah is eternal Creator, eternal knowledge, He does what He wills, He is not questioned, intercession for major sinners is true, punishment of the grave is true, hope in supplication, and others as countable. These define orthodoxy.
The exact list may vary slightly; the key is that belief in these distinguishes a Sunni from an innovator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي السراجية : المؤمن لا يخرج عن الإيمان بارتكاب الكبيرة، وإذا مات بغير توبة فهو في مشيئة الله تعالى إن شاء غفر له وإن شاء عذبه بقدر جنايته أو أقل ثم يدخله الجنة. والقرآن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق ولا محدث، والمكتوب في المصاحف دال على كلام الله تعالى وأنه مخلوق. رؤية الله تعالى في الآخرة حق يراه أهل الجنة في الآخر بلا كيفية ولا تشبيه ولا محازاة، أما رؤية الله تعالى في المنام أكثرهم قالوا لا تجوز والسكوت في هذا الباب أحوط . القدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى بمشيئته وإرادته القديمة إلا أن المعاصي ليست برضا الله تعالى.
وفي الحاوي وعن أبي سلمة الفقيه أنه قال : هذه عشرة مسائل التي وجدت عليها السلف أهل الهداية والجماعة من آمن بها كان منهم، ومن لو يؤمن بها فهو من أهل صاحب هوى وبدعة ثم عد هذه العشرة وقال قال شيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن القاضي : إن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد وأفعالهم بقضاء الله تعالى ومشيئته، وأن الله تعالى خالق لم يزل، وأن الله تعالى له علم موصوف في الأزل، وأن الله تعالى يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد إذا كان أصلح للعباد أو لم يكن لا يسأل عما يفعل وهم يسألون، وأن شفاعة محمد حق لأهل الكبائر من أمته وأن عذاب القبر حق، وأنه يرجى من الله تعالى أن يعطي العباد ما يسألونه من دعائهم.
And in al-Sirajiyyah: The believer does not exit from faith by committing a major sin. If he dies without repentance, he is under Allah's will: if He wills, He forgives him; if He wills, He punishes him according to his crime or less, then enters him into Paradise. The Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated and not originated. What is written in the mus'hafs is indicative of the speech of Allah and it is created. Seeing Allah in the Hereafter is true; the people of Paradise will see Him in the end without modality, without likeness, and without facing. As for seeing Allah in dreams, most scholars said it is not permissible, and silence on this matter is more cautious. Destiny, its good and evil, is from Allah by His eternal will and desire, except that sins are not with Allah's pleasure. And in al-Hawi, from Abu Salama al-Faqih that he said: These are ten issues upon which I found the Salaf, the people of guidance and the community. Whoever believes in them is from them, and whoever does not believe in them is from the people of desire and innovation. Then he listed these ten. He said: Shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Qadi said: Allah created the actions of the servants and their actions are by Allah's decree and will; Allah is ever the Creator; Allah has knowledge described in eternity; Allah does what He wills and judges what He desires, whether it is better for the servants or not; He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked; the intercession of Muhammad is true for the people of major sins from his community; the punishment of the grave is true; and it is hoped from Allah that He gives to the servants what they ask in their supplication.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage presents key Hanafi creedal positions on four major topics: the status of the grave sinner, the Quran, seeing Allah, and destiny. First, the Hanafi view on the grave sinner (murtakib al-kabirah) is that he does not leave the fold of Islam; he remains a believer but is subject to Allah's will – He may forgive him directly or punish him in Hell before entering Paradise. This is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah against the Khawarij (who declare him a disbeliever) and the Mu'tazila (who place him in a middle state). Second, the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah; the written copies (masahif) are created indicators (dall) of that speech. This is a key Hanafi-Maturidi position against the Mu'tazila who claimed the Quran is created. Third, seeing Allah (ru'yah) in the Hereafter is true (haqq) without modality or resemblance to physical sight; seeing Allah in dreams is generally not permissible, and silence is prudent. Fourth, destiny (qadr) with its good and evil is from Allah’s eternal will, but sins are not with His pleasure (rida) – He does not approve of evil. Then the passage lists ten principles of Ahl al-Sunnah from Abu Salama al-Faqih: (1) Allah creates the actions of the servants and their actions are by His decree; (2) Allah is ever the Creator; (3) Allah has eternal knowledge; (4) Allah does what He wills; (5) He is not questioned about His actions; (6) Intercession for major sinners is true; (7) Punishment of the grave is true; (8) Hope that Allah answers supplications (this list may vary slightly in the text). These ten are the foundations of orthodox Sunni belief, distinguishing the follower from the innovator.

Key Terms
الكبيرة (al-kabirah): A major sin that does not expel a believer from faith according to Ahl al-Sunnah.
الرؤية (al-ru'yah): The vision of Allah by the believers in Paradise without modality or direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the grave sinner (murtakib al-kabirah) according to this passage?
A) He becomes a disbeliever and leaves the fold of Islam
B) He remains a believer but will be punished in Hell for eternity
C) He remains a believer, his fate is in Allah's will, and he may eventually enter Paradise
D) He is in a middle state between believer and disbeliever

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi creed teaches that a grave sinner remains a believer, the Quran is uncreated, seeing Allah in the Hereafter is true, and both good and evil are from Allah's will, but He does not approve of sin.

Divine Attributes in Hanafi Creed
Creedal statement on divine attributes and their modality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that all divine attributes are eternal and describe the ruling on using Persian terms for Allah's hand and eye.

Core Idea
All of Allah’s attributes are equally eternal and must be affirmed without modality.

In this passage from al-Sirajiyyah, the Hanafi school lays down its position on Allah’s attributes. The text rejects any distinction between attributes of essence and attributes of action, affirming that all are eternal and subsist in Allah’s essence. It also addresses the sensitive issue of describing Allah with hand and eye, and whether this is permissible in Persian.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on attributes
The text states all attributes are eternal without distinction.
2
Understand the negation of corporealism
Allah is not a body, substance, or accident, nor located in place.
3
Analyze the hand and eye affirmation
Affirmed without modality (bila kayf).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on Persian
Abu Shuja‘ allows 'hand' in Persian but not 'eye'.

علمه أنه يذكر ويخشى ويلزم الحجة على من علم منه أنه لا يؤمن ويأبى، وأن الخيرة فيما قضاه الله وقدره، وأنه يقضي بالحق وأن الرضا بقضائه واجب والتسليم لأمره لازم، وأن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، وأن And in al-Sirajiyyah: All attributes of Allah are eternal, without distinction between attributes of essence and attributes of action, and they subsist in Allah's essence; He is not [like] it nor other than it, like the one from the ten. Allah is not a body, nor substance, nor accident, nor is He in place. Then Allah is described with attributes of perfection, and He is described as having a hand and an eye, but not like the hands or eyes [of creation], and one does not delve into modality. Is it allowed to describe Allah with these two attributes in Persian? Sayyid al-Imam Abu Shuja' said: Regarding the hand it is allowed, but regarding the eye it is not. And in al-Hawi, some of the Salaf said: The correct statement is that the servant, when possible, should say with the naming: 'I believe in all that the Messenger of Allah brought, according to the meaning intended by the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'In my view, I am a believer before Allah.' Some disputants from the theologians mentioned that what is obligatory upon a person is one of two things: either to engage in acquiring this art (theology) until he reaches its utmost so that he becomes sharp enough for debate and argument, or to adhere to what the people of the religion have agreed upon, and avoid sin and zeal for other than religion, and perform the obligations of Allah. The summary statements we have mentioned: Allah is One, no partner, no equal, no likeness; He has always existed before place and time, before the Throne and air, before what He created from that; He is the Eternal and everything else is originated; He is just in His decree, truthful in His news; corruption is not obligatory; He does not approve of disbelief for His servants; He does not burden them beyond capacity; He is wise and good in all His actions in everything He created, decreed, and destined; He intends ease for them and does not intend hardship; He sent messengers and revealed books so that they remember what preceded in His knowledge that they would remember and fear, and the proof is established upon those He knows will not believe and refuse; the choice is in what Allah has decreed and destined; He judges with truth; being pleased with His decree is obligatory and submission to His command is necessary; whatever Allah wills occurs and what He does not will does not; what He decrees is executed among His creation and what He destines is binding upon them; its interpretation is the interpretation of the Muslims; there is no repelling it; His command is effective among His creation, their habit is need of Him in performing what He obligated them, while He is independent; His giving does not harm Him, nor His withholding benefit Him; He created the creation of jinn and humans only to worship Him; He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills; His misguidance is not like the misguidance of the one whom Satan and his party learn; He leads astray the wrongdoers and does not lead astray the corrupt. And in al-Sirajiyyah: Our Prophet is the most noble of creation and the best; his Mi'raj was to the Throne (according to what Allah honored him); the vision of Paradise and Hell is true; the message of the messengers does not become void with their death; the messengers of the children of Adam are better than the entirety of angels; the common believers from the children of Adam who are pious are better than the common angels; the elite of the angels are better than the common children of Adam. The miracles of the saints (karamat al-awliya) are true; the saint is not superior to the prophet; the intercession of the prophets and the righteous for some sinners among the Muslims is true. The best of creation from this Ummah is Abu Bakr ibn Abi Quhafah al-Taymi, then Umar ibn al-Khattab al-'Adawi, then Uthman ibn 'Affan al-Umawi, then Ali ibn Abi Talib al-Hashimi (may Allah be pleased with them all). The condition is that the caliph be Qurashi, and it is not conditioned that he be Hashimi. Justice is not a condition for the validity of imamah and leadership; it is only a condition of preference. Knowledge is better than intellect according to us, contrary to the Mu'tazila. The people of Paradise are secure from removal (or: from punishment? ) but not secure from the fear of argument. The children of polytheists: it is said they are in...
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This lengthy passage covers multiple Hanafi creedal positions. It begins with divine attributes: all attributes are eternal (qadimah) without division into attributes of essence and attributes of action; they subsist in Allah's essence, not separate from Him or identical with Him (like 'one of ten' is a known analogy for attributes neither identical nor separate). Allah is not a body (jism), substance (jawhar), accident ('arad), nor located in place. He is described with hands and eyes but without modality (bila kayf). A notable linguistic ruling: according to Abu Shuja', it is permissible to describe Allah with 'hand' in Persian but not 'eye' – possibly because 'eye' in Persian may imply physical similarity. Then follows the principle of Iman: one should believe in all that the Prophet brought according to the Prophet's intended meaning. Paradise and Hell are eternal (la yafnayan). Abu Hanifa's response to 'are you a believer before Allah?' is 'at my view, I am a believer before Allah', meaning he asserts his Iman subjectively, leaving absolute knowledge to Allah. The passage then gives advice: one must either become a skilled theologian for debate or simply follow the consensus of the Ummah. A comprehensive summary of creed is then presented: tawhid, transcendence, justice in decree, no burden beyond capacity, wisdom in all actions, purpose of sending messengers is to fulfill divine knowledge and establish proof, predestination, pleasure with decree, etc. Notably, Allah's misguidance is not like Satan's misguidance; He misguides the wrongdoers but not the corrupt (possibly a nuance). Then specific points: the Prophet is the best of creation; the Miraj to the Throne (according to some); seeing Paradise and Hell is true; messengers remain messengers even after death (their message is not void); the prophets are superior to all angels; pious common believers are better than common angels; elite angels are better than common believers; miracles of saints are true; saints are not superior to prophets; intercession is true. The best of the Ummah are the four rightly guided caliphs in order of superiority (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali). The caliph must be from Quraysh (not necessarily Hashimi). Justice ('adalah) is not a condition for the validity of imamate or leadership; it is only a condition of preference (meaning an unjust caliph is still caliph). Knowledge is better than intellect, contra the Mu'tazila. Finally, a note about the people of Paradise being secure from 'al-azl' (possibly meaning removal from Paradise) but not secure from fear of argument (jidal) – perhaps meaning they still fear the questioning or judgment before entering. The children of polytheists are mentioned but the sentence is cut off; later texts discuss their fate.

Key Terms
صفات الذات وصفات الفعل (sifat al-dhat wa sifat al-fi'l): Attributes of essence (like life, power) vs. attributes of action (like creating, providing). The text says no distinction is made between them in terms of eternity.
بلا كيف (bila kayf): Without modality; affirming the attribute without asking or explaining how it applies to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Not permissible
C) Permissible for hand but not eye
D) No ruling given

Key Takeaway
All divine attributes are equally eternal; hand and eye are affirmed without modality, with a linguistic caution on Persian.

Ruling on Describing Allah with Hand and Eye in Persian
Question and answer about translating divine attributes into Persian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on translating divine attributes into Persian and explain why the ruling differs for 'hand' versus 'eye'.

Core Idea
It is permissible to describe Allah with 'hand' in Persian but not with 'eye' — the ruling depends on the risk of corporeal understanding.

This lesson addresses a practical question for Persian-speaking Muslims: may they describe Allah in their native language using terms like 'hand' and 'eye'? The Hanafi jurist Imam Abu Shuja' gives a nuanced answer: 'hand' is permissible, but 'eye' is not. We will explore the theological reasoning behind this distinction, grounded in the principle of tanzih (transcendence) and the avoidance of tashbih (anthropomorphism).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two attributes and their Arabic terms
The passage mentions two divine attributes: al-yad (hand) and al-'ayn (eye). Both are affirmed in the Quran and Sunnah, and the Hanafi school affirms them as real attributes of Allah, but without modality (bilā kayf) or resemblance to creation.
The key Arabic terms are اليد (yad) and العين (ayn).
2
Understand the principle of tanzih
The passage opens by stating that Allah is described with attributes of perfection, but 'not like hands nor like eyes, and one does not occupy with modality.' This establishes the creedal foundation: we affirm the attributes while negating any similarity to created things.
Tanzih means declaring Allah free from any imperfection or resemblance.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Shuja's ruling for 'hand'
Imam Abu Shuja' rules that describing Allah with 'hand' in Persian is permissible (يجوز باليد). The likely reason is that the Persian word 'dast' is commonly understood in a metaphorical sense (power, favor), reducing the risk of corporeal imagination.
In Persian, 'dast' (دست) frequently appears in expressions like 'dast-e qudrat' (hand of power), making it less anthropomorphic.
4
Analyze Imam Abu Shuja's ruling for 'eye'
For 'eye', Imam Abu Shuja' rules that it is not permissible (بالعين لا). The Persian word 'chashm' (چشم) is more directly associated with a physical organ of sight, increasing the risk of tashbih. Therefore, it is avoided in describing Allah.
The ruling shows sensitivity to linguistic connotation: 'chashm' in everyday Persian almost always refers to a physical eye.
5
Apply the reasoning to similar attributes
The distinction between yad and 'ayn is a case-specific application of a wider principle: when translating divine attributes into another language, the permissibility depends on whether the translation is likely to lead to a corporeal understanding. Attributes like 'face' (wajh) or 'soul' (nafs) would need similar scrutiny.
This is not a blanket rule for all attributes; each must be evaluated separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية يريد موصوف بصفات الكمال ويوصف بأن له يداً وعيناً ولكن لا كالأيدي ولا كالأعين ولا يشتغل بالكيفية. وهل يجوز وصف الله تعالى بهذين الصفتين بالفارسية؟ قال السيد الإمام أبو شجاع باليد يجوز وبالعين لا.
Book of Dislikes. He intends: He is described with attributes of perfection, and it is described that He has a hand and an eye, but not like hands nor like eyes, and one does not occupy with modality. And is it permissible to describe Allah Almighty with these two attributes in Persian? The master Imam Abu Shuja' said: with 'hand' it is permissible, with 'eye' it is not.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Book of Karahiyya (Disliked Matters) concerning the theological issue of describing Allah with anthropomorphic attributes. The author states that Allah possesses attributes of perfection, including having a hand and an eye, but negates any similarity to created beings (tashbih) and forbids speculation about modality (kayfiyya). The core ruling here is the answer to a practical question: may a Persian-speaking believer describe Allah with these attributes in Persian? The Hanafi jurist Imam Abu Shuja' (likely a reference) responds that describing Allah with 'yad' (hand) in Persian is permissible, but describing Him with 'ayn' (eye) is not. The difference may be due to linguistic or theological sensitivities: 'yad' in Persian (dast) is commonly used for power, while 'ayn' (chashm) may carry more corporeal connotations. This ruling is a creedal one, showing the Hanafi commitment to the principle of tanzih (transcendence) while affirming the attributes mentioned in revelation.

Key Terms
اليد (al-yad): An attribute of Allah affirmed without modality (bilā kayf) and without resemblance to creation.
العين (al-'ayn): An attribute of Allah affirmed similarly to yad, but the ruling differs for Persian translation.
الفارسية (al-farisiyya): The Persian language; the ruling concerns whether it is permissible to use Persian equivalents for these divine attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Not permissible (la yajuz)
C) Obligatory (wajib)
D) Recommended (mandub)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi creed, translating divine attributes into Persian is not uniform: 'hand' is permissible but 'eye' is not, due to the risk of corporeal misunderstanding.

Foundational Creedal Statements of Ahl al-Sunnah
Creedal summary affirming tawhid, attributes, justice, and predestination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the foundational creedal beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah according to the Hanafi school and explain their key implications for divine justice and human responsibility.

Core Idea
Allah is one, just, and wise; His decree is effective, yet humans are accountable and must be content with His will.

This passage presents a concise summary of the essential beliefs (aqidah) agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah as articulated by the Hanafi school. Covering tawhid, divine attributes, justice, predestination, and the purpose of creation, these statements form the bedrock of Islamic creed. Memorizing and internalizing them is crucial for every Muslim, as they guide correct belief and practice in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core themes
Read the passage and list the major themes: Tawhid, Divine Attributes, Divine Justice, Predestination, Human Capacity, Purpose of Creation, and Misguidance.
These themes interconnect to form a coherent worldview.
2
Understand each statement in context
For each theme, note the specific Arabic phrasing and its theological implication. For example, 'la yukallifuhum ma la yutiqun' affirms human capacity.
Pay attention to the nuances in the original language.
3
Connect to Hanafi positions
Recognize how these statements reflect distinct Hanafi stances, such as the doctrine of kasb (acquisition), the obligation of rida bi al-qada (contentment with decree), and the distinction between zalimin and fasiqin.
This helps differentiate Hanafi creed from other theological schools.
4
Memorize the key phrases
Commit the essential Arabic phrases to memory. These include: 'الله واحد لا شريك له', 'الخيرة فيما قضاه الله', 'الرضا بقضائه واجب', 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن', and 'خلق الخلق إلا ليعبدوه'.
Memorization anchors the creed for recitation and reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجمل التي ذكرناها أن الله تعالى واحد لا شريك له ولا مثيل له ولا شبيه له، وأنه لم يزل قبل المكان والزمان وقبل العرش والهواء وقبل ما خلق من ذلك موجوداً، وأنه القديم وما سواه محدث، وأنه العادل في قضائه الصادق في أخباره، ولا يجب الفساد، ولا يرضى لعباده الكفر، وأنه لا يكلفهم ما لا يطيقون وأنه حكيم وحسن في جميع أفعاله في كل ما خلق وقضى وقدر، وأنه بهم اليسر ولا يريد بهم العسر، أنه إنما بعث إليهم المرسلين وأنزل عليهم الكتب ليذكر ما وقع في سابق علمه أنه يذكر ويخشى ويلزم الحجة على من علم منه أنه لا يؤمن ويأبى، وأن الخيرة فيما قضاه الله وقدره، وأنه يقضي بالحق وأن الرضا بقضائه واجب والتسليم لأمره لازم، وأن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، وأن ما قضى فهو ماض في خلقه، وما قدر فهو لازم لهم، وأن تأويل ذلك هو تأويل المسلمين، وأنه لا مرد له، وأن أمره نافذ في خلقه دأبهم الحاجة إليه في أداء ما كلفهم به وهو غني عنه لا يضره بذله ولا ينفعه منعه، وأنه ما خلق الخلق من الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدوه وأنه يضل من يشاء ويهدي من شاء وأن إضلاله ليس كإضلال الذي علم به الشيطان وحزبه، وأنه يضل الظالمين ولا يضل الفاسقين.
And the statements that we have mentioned: that Allah Almighty is one, no partner, no likeness, no similitude to Him; that He has always existed before place and time and before the Throne and the air and before what He created of that, existing; that He is the Eternal and everything else is originated; that He is just in His decree, truthful in His reports, He does not will corruption, He does not approve for His servants disbelief; that He does not burden them beyond their capacity; that He is wise and good in all His actions in everything He created, decreed, and predestined; that He intends ease for them and does not intend hardship; that He only sent messengers to them and revealed books to them so that what had occurred in His prior knowledge would be remembered and feared, and to establish the proof against those whom He knows will not believe and will refuse; that the choice is in what God decreed and predestined; that He judges with truth, and contentment with His decree is obligatory and submission to His command is necessary; that whatever God wills occurs, and whatever He does not will does not occur; that whatever He decrees is executed in His creation, and whatever He predestines is necessary for them; that the interpretation of that is the interpretation of the Muslims; that there is no repeller for it; that His command is effective in His creation; their consistent need is for Him in performing what He charged them with, while He is independent of them; His giving does not harm Him nor does His withholding benefit Him; that He created the creation of jinn and humans only to worship Him; that He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills; that His misguidance is not like the misguidance of which Satan and his party know; and that He leads wrongdoers astray and does not lead the disobedient astray.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a creedal summary (aqidah) of the foundational beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah according to the Hanafi school. It is a compilation of statements (jumal) that have been mentioned earlier in the text. The passage covers key articles: Tawhid (absolute oneness), pre-existence of Allah before all creation, justice (adl) in His actions, truthfulness of His reports, rejection of the idea that Allah wills evil or approves disbelief, human capacity limited to what Allah gives, wisdom and goodness in all divine acts, purpose of sending messengers and books, predestination and the necessity of contentment (rida bi al-qada), the effective nature of divine will, and the purpose of creation (worship). It also addresses the issue of misguidance (idlaal): that Allah misguides the wrongdoers (zalimin) but not the disobedient (fasiqin) – this is a nuanced position distinguishing between those who are unjust and those who merely sin. The passage establishes the Hanafi position on qadr: both good and evil are by divine decree, but Allah does not approve of evil. The believer must believe in these tenets without delving into speculative theology (kalam) beyond what is necessary.

Key Terms
الخيرة (al-khayyira): Choice or power of choice; the text says 'al-khayyira fima qadah Allah' meaning that the ultimate choice rests in what God decrees.
الرضا بقضائه (al-rida bi qada'ihi): Contentment with Allah's decree; this is obligatory (wajib) in the Hanafi creed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the purpose for which Allah created jinn and humans?
A) To benefit from their worship
B) Only to worship Him
C) To populate the earth
D) To test them

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi creed affirms divine oneness, justice, and wisdom, while maintaining human responsibility and the necessity of contentment with Allah's decree.

Prophetic Superiority, Angelic Ranks, and Karamat
A series of creedal rulings on ranks of prophets, angels, and saints

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the superiority of prophets over angels and the reality of karamat al-awliya.

Core Idea
Prophets are superior to all angels; pious believers outrank common angels, but elite angels surpass common believers.

This passage from al-Sirajiyya presents foundational creedal rulings about the spiritual hierarchy. The Hanafi school distinguishes between categories of angels and humans, affirming the unique rank of prophets while also honouring the awliya and their miracles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary claim about Prophetic superiority
The passage states that our Prophet (ﷺ) is the most honourable, and messengers among humans are better than the entire host of angels. Note that this applies to all prophets.
2
Distinguish categories of angels and humans
The text divides angels into common and elite, and humans into messengers, pious common believers, and sinful believers. The ranking varies: messengers > all angels; pious believers > common angels; elite angels > common believers.
This is a nuanced position unique to Hanafis.
3
Understand karamat and intercession
Karamat (miracles of saints) are affirmed but no saint surpasses a prophet. Intercession is also affirmed for sinful Muslims.
4
Note the epistemological basis
These are transmitted rulings from al-Sirajiyya, a Hanafi text; they are creedal (i'tiqadi) but treated as necessary knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي السراجية : نبينا أكرم الخلق وأفضلهم، ومعراجه إلى العرش إلى ما أكرمه الله تعالى، ورؤية الجنة والنار حق، ورسالة الرسل لا تبطل بموتهم ، ورسل بني آدم أفضل من جملة الملائكة، وعوام بني آدم من الأتقياء أفضل من عوام الملائكة، وخواص الملائكة أفضل من عوام بني آدم . كرامة الأولياء حق، والولي لا يكون أفضل من النبي، وشفاعة الأنبياء والصالحين لبعض العصاة من المسلمين حق، وأفضل الخليقة من هذه الأمة أبو بكر بن أبي قحافة التيمي، ثم عمر بن العدوي، ثم . عثمان بن عفان الأموي، ثم علي بن أبي طالب الهاشمي رضوان الله تعالى عليهم أجمعين . الشرط أن يكون الخليفة قرشياً ولا يشترط أن يكون هاشمياً. العدالة ليست شرطاً لصحة الإمامة والإمارة والقضاة إنما هي شرط الأولوية . العلم أفضل من العقل عندنا خلافاً للمعتزلة .
And in al-Sirajiyya: Our prophet is the most honourable of creation and the best of them; his mi'raj was to the Throne to what Allah honoured him; vision of Paradise and Hellfire is true; the message of messengers does not become void upon their death; the messengers of the children of Adam are better than the entire host of angels; the common believers among the children of Adam who are pious are better than the common angels; the elite of the angels are better than the common believers of the children of Adam. The miracle of awliya is true; a wali is not superior to a prophet; intercession of prophets and righteous people for some sinful Muslims is true. The best of creation from this ummah is Abu Bakr ibn Abi Quhafa al-Taymi, then Umar ibn al-Adawi, then Uthman ibn Affan al-Umawi, then Ali ibn Abi Talib al-Hashimi, may Allah be pleased with them all. The condition is that the caliph be Qurayshi, and it is not required that he be Hashimi. Uprightness ('adala) is not a condition for the validity of leadership (imama), government, and judges; rather it is a condition of preference. Knowledge is better than intellect according to us, contrary to the Mu'tazila.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage presents a series of creedal rulings (masa'il i'tiqadiyya) from the work al-Sirajiyya. It covers: (1) The superiority of our Prophet Muhammad ﷺ over all creation. (2) His ascension (mi'raj) was bodily to the Throne. (3) Seeing Paradise and Hellfire in the afterlife is a reality. (4) The prophethood of messengers does not end with their death; they remain prophets. (5) Messengers among humans are superior to all angels collectively (jummala), meaning as a group. (6) Pious common believers are superior to common angels, but (7) the elite angels (such as Jibril) are superior to common believers. This is the Hanafi position: the superiority (afdaliyya) varies by category. (8) Miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya) are true, but (9) no saint can exceed a prophet in rank. (10) Intercession (shafa'a) by prophets and righteous people for sinful Muslims is true. (11) The best of the ummah after the Prophet are the four Rightly Guided Caliphs in order: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali – this is the Hanafi and Sunni position, affirming the superiority of Abu Bakr. (12) The caliph must be from the tribe of Quraysh, but not necessarily from the Banu Hashim (as the Shia claim). (13) 'Adala (uprightness) is not a condition for the validity of the imam's authority, but it is a condition for his preference (i.e., it is better to have a just imam). (14) Knowledge (ilm) is superior to mere intellect (aql), contrary to the Mu'tazila who prioritize reason.

Key Terms
السراجية (al-Sirajiyya): A Hanafi fiqh work; used here for creedal statements.
الكرامة (al-karama): Supernatural events granted by Allah to His awliya (saints) as honor, not as proof of prophethood.
القرشي (al-qurashi): A condition for the caliph: he must be from the tribe of Quraysh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is superior?
A) Common angels are superior to pious believers.
B) Pious believers are superior to common angels.
C) Elite angels are inferior to common believers.
D) All angels are equal in rank to all believers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms a nuanced hierarchy: prophets are superior to all angels, pious believers outrank common angels, but elite angels surpass common believers.

The Four Caliphs and the Conditions of Khilafah
Rulings on the order of the caliphs and conditions of leadership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the order of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and the conditions for the caliph.

Core Idea
The caliph must be Qurayshi, but not necessarily Hashimi; uprightness is preferred but not required for validity.

This passage continues with the order of the four caliphs by virtue and outlines key conditions for the legitimacy of the caliph, including lineage and moral uprightness. Understanding these rulings clarifies the Hanafi view on political leadership.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the order of the caliphs
The text lists Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali as the best of the ummah after the Prophet. This order is a matter of creed for Hanafis.
This is a Sunni consensus.
2
Identify the condition of Quraysh
The caliph must be from Quraysh. This condition is based on the statement of the Prophet (ﷺ) and the consensus of the Sahaba.
It is not required that he be from Banu Hashim.
3
Understand the role of 'adala
Uprightness ('adala) is not a condition for the validity of the imam's authority; it is only a condition for preference. An unjust imam remains legitimate.
4
Learn the superiority of knowledge over intellect
The passage concludes that knowledge ('ilm) is better than mere intellect (aql), refuting the Mu'tazila who prioritize reason.

Children of Polytheists: Tawaqquf and Its Implications
Creedal ruling on children of polytheists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the fate of children of polytheists and explain the reasoning behind tawaqquf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa suspended judgment on children of polytheists; later Hanafis ruled they follow their parents.

This lesson examines a subtle creedal issue: the fate of children who die before reaching maturity, whose parents were polytheists. The Hanafi school presents two views—the earlier suspension of judgment (tawaqquf) by Abu Hanifa and the later position that such children are considered disbelievers. Understanding the methodological basis for tawaqquf is key to appreciating Hanafi caution in the absence of decisive textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
From the text, note that some scholars said children of polytheists are in Paradise, others said Hell. Then note Abu Hanifa's unique position: tawaqquf (suspension). Finally, note al-Radi's later ruling that the child of a disbeliever is a disbeliever.
There is no explicit Quranic or Hadith text decisive on this matter.
2
Analyze the basis for tawaqquf
Tawaqquf means neither affirming Paradise nor Hell for these children. The Hanafi principle is that where textual evidence is absent or conflicting, one suspends judgment. The absence of clear addressing of this age group leaves the matter to Allah's mercy and justice.
Tawaqquf is a legitimate position in usul al-fiqh when evidence is inconclusive.
3
Contrast with al-Radi's view
Al-Imam al-Radi ruled that the child of a disbeliever is a disbeliever, meaning they follow the religion of their parents. This is based on the general principle that children inherit the status of their parents until they reach maturity and choose for themselves.
This view aligns with the majority of later Hanafis and is used in fatwa.
4
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
While Abu Hanifa's tawaqquf is recorded, the later relied-upon position is that children of disbelievers are considered disbelievers. This is the view adopted for legal purposes, e.g., inheritance and funeral rulings.
This illustrates how later tarjih can supersede the founder's view when evidence is clearer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهل الجنة آمنون عن العزل غير آمنين عن خوف الجدال أطفال المشركين قيل هم في الجنة وقيل هم في النار وأبو حنيفة توقف فيهم. وقال الشيخ الإمام الرضي: إن ولد الكافر كافر . الكلام في الروح قال بعضهم يجوز ، وقال بعضهم لا يجوز ، ثم قيل هي الحياة، وقيل هي عرض، وقيل إنها جسم لطيف وهي ريح مخصوص . سؤال منكر ونكير حق وسؤالهما الأنبياء قيل بهذه العبارة على ماذا تركتم أمتكم. وفي بستان الفقيه باب ما جاء في ذكر الحفظة قال الفقيه : اختلف الفقهاء في أمر الحفظة الكرام الكتابين ؛ قال بعضهم يكتبون جميع أقوال بني آدم وأفعالهم، وقال بعضهم لا يكتبون إلا ما فيه أجر أو إثم. ثم قال بعضهم: يكتبون الجميع فإذا صعدوا السماء حذفوا ما لا أجر فيه ولا إثم وقال هو معنى قوله تعالى يمحوا الله ما يشاء ويثبت [الرعد: ۳۹] قال ابن جريج : هما ملكان أحدهما عن يمينه والآخر عن شماله، فالذي عن يمينه يكتب بغير شهادة صاحبه والذي عن يساره لا يكتب إلا بشهادة منه إن قعد قعد الحفظة واحد عن يمينه والآخر عن يساره، وإن مشى فأحدهما أمامه والآخر خلفه، وإن نام فأحدهما عند رأسه والآخر عند رجليه وقال بعضهم أربعة اثنان بالنهار واثنان بالليل والخامس لا يفارقه ليلاً ولا نهاراً واختلف الناس في الكفرة قال بعضهم عليهم حفظة، وقال بعضهم لا يكون عليهم حفظة لأن أمرهم فرط وعليهم .واحد قال الفقيه : لا يؤخذ بهذا القول والآية نزلت بذكر الحفظة في شأن الكفار . (تتمة : سئل بعضهم هل على الصبي حفظة يكتبون له؟ فقال: رفع القلم عن ثلاث . قيل له : هل يكون معذوراً بترك النظر؟ قيل : استكمال المدة التي يتعلق بها أحكام الشرع فقال : إن كمل شرائط تكليفه قبل البلوغ وخطر بباله الخوف من ترك النظر لا يعذر. وفي السراجية : عذاب القبر للكافرين أو لبعض العصاة حق يؤمن به ولا يشتغل بكيفيته.
The people of Paradise are secure from removal? Not secure from fear of argument? The children of polytheists: some said they are in Paradise, some said they are in Hellfire, and Abu Hanifa suspended judgment concerning them. And al-Shaykh al-Imam al-Radi said: indeed the child of a disbeliever is a disbeliever. Speech concerning the soul: some said it is permissible, some said it is not permissible. Then it was said it is life, said it is an accident, said it is a subtle body and it is a specific wind. The questioning of Munkar and Nakir is true, and their questioning of the prophets - it is said with this expression: 'What did you leave your ummah upon?' And in Bustan al-Faqih, chapter on the mention of the guarding angels (hafazah). Al-Faqih said: The jurists differed concerning the matter of the noble recording angels: some said they write all the statements and actions of the children of Adam, and some said they only write what contains reward or sin. Then some said: they write everything, then when they ascend to heaven they delete what contains no reward nor sin, and it is said that is the meaning of His statement: 'Allah erases what He wills and affirms' [13:39]. Ibn Jurayj said: They are two angels, one on his right and the other on his left; the one on his right writes without the testimony of his companion, and the one on his left does not write except with testimony from him. If he sits, the guardians sit one on his right and the other on his left; if he walks, one is in front of him and the other behind him; if he sleeps, one is at his head and the other at his feet. Some said four: two by day and two by night, and a fifth does not leave him night or day. People differed concerning the disbelievers: some said they have guardians, some said they do not have guardians because their matter is overlooked, and upon them is one. Al-Faqih said: This statement is not to be taken, and the verse was revealed mentioning the guardians concerning the disbelievers. (Appendix: He was asked: Are there guardians for a child who write for him? He said: The pen is lifted from three. He was asked: Is he excused for abandoning consideration (al-nazar)? He said: Completion of the period by which the rulings of the law are attached. He said: If he has fulfilled the conditions of his responsibility before puberty and fear passes his mind of abandoning consideration, he is not excused. And in al-Sirajiyya: The punishment of the grave for the disbelievers or for some of the disobedient is true; one believes in it and does not occupy himself with its modality.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage covers several distinct creedal rulings. Firstly, the fate of children of polytheists (atfal al-mushrikin): there is a difference of opinion; some say they are in Paradise, some say in Hell, and Imam Abu Hanifa withheld judgment (tawaqquf). However, al-Imam al-Radi (a Hanafi authority) rules that the child of a disbeliever is a disbeliever (i.e., follows the parent's religion). Secondly, the soul (ruh): some permit discussing it, some do not. Various views are mentioned: the soul is life (hayat), an accident (arad), a subtle body (jism latif) and a specific wind (rih makhsus). The Hanafi position tends to affirm the soul is a created subtle body. Thirdly, the questioning of Munkar and Nakir in the grave is true. The angels' questioning of prophets is reported in a specific wording: 'What did you leave your ummah upon?' indicating they are asked about their community. Fourthly, a discussion from Bustan al-Faqih on the recording angels (hafazah). The jurists differed: some say they record all actions and words; others say only those with reward or sin. A third view says they record everything, then upon ascent delete the neutral ones, citing Quran 13:39. The physical arrangement of the angels is described: one on the right, one on the left; the right records without witness, the left requires witness. Others say four angels (two day, two night) plus a fifth constant angel. For disbelievers, there is difference: some say they have guardians (i.e., angels record their deeds), others say not because their matter is 'farat' (i.e., they are neglected?) but al-Faqih rejects this view, saying the verse about guardians was revealed concerning disbelievers. An appendix discusses whether children (non-pubescent) have recording angels: the pen is lifted from three (the minor, the sleeping, the insane). But if the minor's conditions of responsibility are complete before puberty (i.e., he is discerning) and he fears abandoning consideration (al-nazar, i.e., reflection on faith), then he is not excused. Finally, from al-Sirajiyya: punishment of the grave is a reality for disbelievers and some sinful Muslims; it is obligatory to believe in it without speculating on its modality (kayfiyya).

Key Terms
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment; Abu Hanifa's position on children of polytheists.
كافر (kafir): Disbeliever; the later Hanafi ruling for a child of polytheists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was Abu Hanifa's position on children of polytheists?
A) They are in Paradise
B) They are in Hell
C) He suspended judgment
D) They are disbelievers

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa suspended judgment on the fate of polytheist children; later Hanafis ruled they follow their parents' disbelief for worldly matters.

6 min
The Soul: Created Subtle Body
Creedal definition of the soul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi view on the nature of the soul as a created subtle body and distinguish it from other opinions.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school affirms the soul is a created subtle body, not an accident, and discussion is permissible.

The nature of the soul (ruh) is a subtle theological issue. The passage records a difference of opinion on whether discussing it is allowed, and then presents various definitions: life, accident, or subtle body. The Hanafi position, which aligns with the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah, is that the soul is a created subtle body and a specific 'wind' (rih makhsus). This lesson unpacks the text and places it within the broader creedal framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissibility of discussion
The text reports two views: some allow discussing the soul, some do not. The Hanafi school does not prohibit it; in fact, they engage in such discussions, as seen here.
The prohibition may stem from the verse 'Say: The soul is of the command of my Lord' (17:85). Hanafis interpret this as it being beyond complete human comprehension, not as a ban on all discussion.
2
Examine the definitions presented
The text lists three views: the soul is life (hayat), an accident (arad), or a subtle body (jism latif) and a specific wind. The first two are rejected by the Hanafi school.
Life is an attribute, not a substance; an accident cannot exist independently.
3
Confirm the Hanafi position
The phrase 'and it is said it is a subtle body and a specific wind' indicates the favored view. This is the position of the Hanafi school: the soul is a created, subtle body that permeates the body, and it is a special type of wind.
This aligns with the Ash'ari position that the soul is a jism latif.
4
Understand the legal effect
Believing in the soul's createdness and distinctness from the body has implications for understanding life, death, and the afterlife. For example, the soul's punishment in the grave requires it to be a substance capable of experiencing sensation.
This connects to the later lesson on grave questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهل الجنة آمنون عن العزل غير آمنين عن خوف الجدال أطفال المشركين قيل هم في الجنة وقيل هم في النار وأبو حنيفة توقف فيهم. وقال الشيخ الإمام الرضي: إن ولد الكافر كافر . الكلام في الروح قال بعضهم يجوز ، وقال بعضهم لا يجوز ، ثم قيل هي الحياة، وقيل هي عرض، وقيل إنها جسم لطيف وهي ريح مخصوص . سؤال منكر ونكير حق وسؤالهما الأنبياء قيل بهذه العبارة على ماذا تركتم أمتكم. وفي بستان الفقيه باب ما جاء في ذكر الحفظة قال الفقيه : اختلف الفقهاء في أمر الحفظة الكرام الكتابين ؛ قال بعضهم يكتبون جميع أقوال بني آدم وأفعالهم، وقال بعضهم لا يكتبون إلا ما فيه أجر أو إثم. ثم قال بعضهم: يكتبون الجميع فإذا صعدوا السماء حذفوا ما لا أجر فيه ولا إثم وقال هو معنى قوله تعالى يمحوا الله ما يشاء ويثبت [الرعد: ۳۹] قال ابن جريج : هما ملكان أحدهما عن يمينه والآخر عن شماله، فالذي عن يمينه يكتب بغير شهادة صاحبه والذي عن يساره لا يكتب إلا بشهادة منه إن قعد قعد الحفظة واحد عن يمينه والآخر عن يساره، وإن مشى فأحدهما أمامه والآخر خلفه، وإن نام فأحدهما عند رأسه والآخر عند رجليه وقال بعضهم أربعة اثنان بالنهار واثنان بالليل والخامس لا يفارقه ليلاً ولا نهاراً واختلف الناس في الكفرة قال بعضهم عليهم حفظة، وقال بعضهم لا يكون عليهم حفظة لأن أمرهم فرط وعليهم .واحد قال الفقيه : لا يؤخذ بهذا القول والآية نزلت بذكر الحفظة في شأن الكفار . (تتمة : سئل بعضهم هل على الصبي حفظة يكتبون له؟ فقال: رفع القلم عن ثلاث . قيل له : هل يكون معذوراً بترك النظر؟ قيل : استكمال المدة التي يتعلق بها أحكام الشرع فقال : إن كمل شرائط تكليفه قبل البلوغ وخطر بباله الخوف من ترك النظر لا يعذر. وفي السراجية : عذاب القبر للكافرين أو لبعض العصاة حق يؤمن به ولا يشتغل بكيفيته.
The people of Paradise are secure from removal? Not secure from fear of argument? The children of polytheists: some said they are in Paradise, some said they are in Hellfire, and Abu Hanifa suspended judgment concerning them. And al-Shaykh al-Imam al-Radi said: indeed the child of a disbeliever is a disbeliever. Speech concerning the soul: some said it is permissible, some said it is not permissible. Then it was said it is life, said it is an accident, said it is a subtle body and it is a specific wind. The questioning of Munkar and Nakir is true, and their questioning of the prophets - it is said with this expression: 'What did you leave your ummah upon?' And in Bustan al-Faqih, chapter on the mention of the guarding angels (hafazah). Al-Faqih said: The jurists differed concerning the matter of the noble recording angels: some said they write all the statements and actions of the children of Adam, and some said they only write what contains reward or sin. Then some said: they write everything, then when they ascend to heaven they delete what contains no reward nor sin, and it is said that is the meaning of His statement: 'Allah erases what He wills and affirms' [13:39]. Ibn Jurayj said: They are two angels, one on his right and the other on his left; the one on his right writes without the testimony of his companion, and the one on his left does not write except with testimony from him. If he sits, the guardians sit one on his right and the other on his left; if he walks, one is in front of him and the other behind him; if he sleeps, one is at his head and the other at his feet. Some said four: two by day and two by night, and a fifth does not leave him night or day. People differed concerning the disbelievers: some said they have guardians, some said they do not have guardians because their matter is overlooked, and upon them is one. Al-Faqih said: This statement is not to be taken, and the verse was revealed mentioning the guardians concerning the disbelievers. (Appendix: He was asked: Are there guardians for a child who write for him? He said: The pen is lifted from three. He was asked: Is he excused for abandoning consideration (al-nazar)? He said: Completion of the period by which the rulings of the law are attached. He said: If he has fulfilled the conditions of his responsibility before puberty and fear passes his mind of abandoning consideration, he is not excused. And in al-Sirajiyya: The punishment of the grave for the disbelievers or for some of the disobedient is true; one believes in it and does not occupy himself with its modality.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage covers several distinct creedal rulings. Firstly, the fate of children of polytheists (atfal al-mushrikin): there is a difference of opinion; some say they are in Paradise, some say in Hell, and Imam Abu Hanifa withheld judgment (tawaqquf). However, al-Imam al-Radi (a Hanafi authority) rules that the child of a disbeliever is a disbeliever (i.e., follows the parent's religion). Secondly, the soul (ruh): some permit discussing it, some do not. Various views are mentioned: the soul is life (hayat), an accident (arad), a subtle body (jism latif) and a specific wind (rih makhsus). The Hanafi position tends to affirm the soul is a created subtle body. Thirdly, the questioning of Munkar and Nakir in the grave is true. The angels' questioning of prophets is reported in a specific wording: 'What did you leave your ummah upon?' indicating they are asked about their community. Fourthly, a discussion from Bustan al-Faqih on the recording angels (hafazah). The jurists differed: some say they record all actions and words; others say only those with reward or sin. A third view says they record everything, then upon ascent delete the neutral ones, citing Quran 13:39. The physical arrangement of the angels is described: one on the right, one on the left; the right records without witness, the left requires witness. Others say four angels (two day, two night) plus a fifth constant angel. For disbelievers, there is difference: some say they have guardians (i.e., angels record their deeds), others say not because their matter is 'farat' (i.e., they are neglected?) but al-Faqih rejects this view, saying the verse about guardians was revealed concerning disbelievers. An appendix discusses whether children (non-pubescent) have recording angels: the pen is lifted from three (the minor, the sleeping, the insane). But if the minor's conditions of responsibility are complete before puberty (i.e., he is discerning) and he fears abandoning consideration (al-nazar, i.e., reflection on faith), then he is not excused. Finally, from al-Sirajiyya: punishment of the grave is a reality for disbelievers and some sinful Muslims; it is obligatory to believe in it without speculating on its modality (kayfiyya).

Key Terms
الروح (al-ruh): The soul; a created subtle body and specific wind.
جسم لطيف (jism latif): Subtle body; the Hanafi definition of the soul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi view on the nature of the soul?
A) It is life
B) It is an accident
C) It is a subtle body and a specific wind
D) Discussion is forbidden

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines the soul as a created subtle body and a specific wind, and considers discussion permissible.

intermediate

Grave Questioning, Recording Angels, and Punishment of the Grave
Creedal rulings on grave events and recording angels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the recording angels for disbelievers, the reality of grave questioning, and the ruling on a child's accountability.

Core Idea
All humans, including disbelievers and discerning minors, have recording angels; grave questioning and punishment are true.

This lesson covers three interconnected topics: the reality of the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, the function and allocation of recording angels (hafazah), and the punishment of the grave. The passage from Bustan al-Faqih clarifies that disbelievers also have guardians who record their deeds, contrary to some scholars. An appendix addresses whether a minor has recording angels and when they become accountable. The final part affirms grave punishment for disbelievers and sinful Muslims, cautioning against speculation on its modality.

Guided Path
1
Affirm the truth of grave questioning
The passage begins: 'The questioning of Munkar and Nakir is true.' This is a foundational belief for Ahl al-Sunnah. The text then notes that prophets are asked about their Ummah.
Belief in the grave questioning is wajib; the modality is not known.
2
Analyze the difference on recording angels
Al-Faqih reports a difference: some say angels record all actions, others only those with reward/sin. A third view is that they record all, then delete neutral ones upon ascent, interpreting 'Allah erases what He wills' (13:39).
The deletion view reconciles the two extremes.
3
Understand the arrangement of angels
Ibn Jurayj describes two angels by day/night, but says they behave differently when sitting, walking, sleeping. Another view says four angels (two day, two night) plus a fifth constant one.
These are detailed reports; the core belief is that record is kept.
4
Determine the ruling on disbelievers' angels
Some said disbelievers have no guardians because their matter is 'farat' (neglected). Al-Faqih rejects this, citing the verse (13:39) revealed about disbelievers, proving they do have guardians.
This is a dispute mapped in the analytical toolbox.
5
Clarify the minor's status and grave punishment
The appendix: the pen is lifted from three (minor, sleeping, insane). But for a discerning minor who fears abandoning reflection, the exemption may be lifted. The punishment of the grave is true for disbelievers and some sinful Muslims; one believes without asking 'how'.
This shows that even a minor can be accountable if conditions are met.

منكر ونكير (Munkar wa Nakir): The two angels who question the dead in the grave.
الحفظة (al-hafazah): The guardian angels who record deeds.

beginner

The Ten Signs of Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah
Hadith listing ten signs of being upon the Sunnah and Jama'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten signs of being upon the Sunnah and Jama'ah as narrated in the hadith of Ibn Umar and explain how each sign distinguishes Sunni theology and practice.

Core Idea
Ten practical signs reveal whether a person is truly upon the Sunnah and Jama'ah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq concludes a chapter on creed with a practical checklist. The hadith of Ibn Umar gives ten concrete indicators that a person is upon the Sunnah. These range from communal prayer and respect for the Companions to theological positions on predestination and not declaring Muslims disbelievers for sins. The Hanafi school particularly emphasizes some of these, such as wiping over khuffs and praying behind any imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authority
Recognize that the hadith is narrated by Abdullah ibn Umar (ra), a companion known for his piety and adherence to the Sunnah. This gives the list strong authority as a sahih transmission.
The hadith is categorized as ahad (single-narrator), so its thubut is zanni, but its content is widely accepted by Ahl al-Sunnah.
2
List the ten signs
Memorize the ten items in order: (1) praying the five prayers in congregation; (2) not speaking ill of any Sahabi; (3) not rebelling against the ruler with the sword; (4) not doubting one's faith; (5) believing in qadr (destiny) from Allah; (6) not arguing in religion; (7) not declaring a Muslim a disbeliever due to sin; (8) not abandoning prayer over deceased Muslims; (9) considering mash 'ala al-khuffayn permissible; (10) praying behind any imam, righteous or wicked.
These ten cover theology, practice, and social ethics.
3
Categorize each sign
Group the signs into categories: theological (4,5,6,7), ritual (1,9,10), social/communal (2,3,8). This helps understand the comprehensive nature of the Sunnah.
Hanafis particularly emphasize items 7, 9, and 10 as distinctive markers against Kharijite and Shia positions.
4
Note the Hanafi emphasis
Identify which signs are especially championed by the Hanafi school: (9) mash 'ala al-khuffayn is a key Sunni practice denied by Shia; (10) praying behind any imam affirms the legitimacy of rulers and refutes rebellion; (7) not takfir of sinners is a core Hanafi principle.
These show how the Hanafi school positions itself as the moderate mainstream.
5
Apply as a self-check
Use this list to evaluate one's own adherence to the Sunnah. For each sign, ask: Do I practice this? Do I hold this belief? This makes the abstract concept of 'Sunnah' concrete.
The hadith itself is a tool for self-awareness, not for judging others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يتصل به فصل يشتمل على السنة والجماعة المضمرات وروي عن علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه قال : المؤمن إذا أوجب السنة والجماعة استجاب الله دعاءه وقضى حوائجه وغفر له الذنوب جميعاً وكتب له براءة من النار وبراءة من النفاق. وفي خبر عبد الله بن عمر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : كان على السنة والجماعة استجاب الله دعاءه وكتب له بكل خطوة من يخطوها عشر حسنات ورفع له عشر درجات فقيل له : يا رسول الله متى يعلم الرجل أنه أهل السنة والجماعة ؟ فقال : إذا وجد في نفسه عشرة أشياء فهو على السنة الجماعة : أن يصلي الصلوات الخمس بالجماعة، ولا يذكر أحداً من الصحابة بسوء وينقصه، ولا يخرج على السلطان بالسيف، ولا يشك في إيمانه، ويؤمن بالقدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى، ولا يجادل في دين الله تعالى، ولا يكفر أحداً من أهل التوحيد بذنب، ولا يدع الصلاة على من من أهل القبلة، ويرى المسح على الخفين جائزاً في السفر والحضر، ويصلي خلف كل إمام براً وفاجر. وفي الحاوي : من أهل السنة والجماعة من فيه عشرة أشياء، : الأول أن لا يقول من مات
And related to it is a chapter comprising the Sunnah and the Jama'ah, the implied matters. It is narrated from Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: The believer, if he actualizes the Sunnah and the Jama'ah, Allah will answer his supplication, fulfill his needs, forgive all his sins, and write for him a certificate of freedom from Hellfire and a certificate of freedom from hypocrisy. And in the report of Abdullah ibn Umar from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: Whoever is upon the Sunnah and the Jama'ah, Allah will answer his supplication, and for every step he takes, write for him ten good deeds and raise him ten degrees. It was said: O Messenger of Allah, when does a man know that he is from Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah? He said: If he finds in himself ten things, then he is upon the Sunnah and the Jama'ah: that he prays the five prayers in congregation, does not mention any Companion of the Prophet with evil and does not detract from them, does not rebel against the ruler with the sword, does not doubt his faith, believes in destiny - its good and evil - from Allah Almighty, does not argue in the religion of Allah Almighty, does not declare any of the people of Tawhid a disbeliever due to a sin, does not abandon prayer over anyone who dies among the people of the Qibla, considers wiping over the khuffs permissible in travel and residence, and prays behind every imam, whether righteous or wicked. And in al-Hawi: He is from Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah who has ten things: the first: that he does not say about one who has died...
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage concludes the section on creed with practical criteria for identifying a person as belonging to Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah. It begins with a saying of Ali (ra) promising immense rewards for one who upholds the Sunnah and the Jama'ah: answered prayers, fulfilled needs, forgiveness of all sins, and freedom from Hell and hypocrisy. Then a hadith from Ibn Umar (ra) lists ten specific characteristics that indicate one is upon the Sunnah and the Jama'ah. These are: (1) performing the five daily prayers in congregation; (2) not speaking ill of any Sahabi or diminishing their status; (3) not rebelling against the Muslim ruler with armed force; (4) not doubting one's own faith (iman); (5) believing in predestination (qadr) that both good and evil come from Allah; (6) not engaging in disputation about religious matters; (7) not declaring any person who professes Tawhid (i.e., Muslims) a disbeliever because of a sin; (8) not abandoning prayer over someone who dies among the people of the Qibla (i.e., Muslims); (9) considering wiping over leather socks (khuffs) as permissible both while traveling and at home; and (10) praying behind any imam, whether righteous or sinful. The final line from al-Hawi gives another list of ten, but the text cuts off at 'the first: that he does not say about one who has died...' likely referring to not declaring a deceased Muslim definitively as in Paradise or Hell. This passage underlines the Hanafi commitment to community unity, avoidance of sectarianism, and adherence to Sunni theology and practice.

Key Terms
السنة والجماعة (al-sunnah wa al-jama'ah): The path of the Prophet and the consensus of the companions; the technical term for the orthodox Sunni community.
أهل التوحيد (ahl al-tawhid): People who profess the oneness of God; i.e., all Muslims.
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks during ablution as a substitute for washing feet. A distinctive practice of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Ten Conditions of Ahl al-Sunnah and Validity of Prayer Behind a Sinner
Lists ten conditions of Ahl al-Sunnah and discusses prayer validity behind sinners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten conditions of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain why prayer behind a sinful Muslim is valid based on the principle of not excommunicating sinners.

Core Idea
A Muslim does not leave Islam by sin; prayer behind a sinful imam is valid and preserves community unity.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq defines the core beliefs and practices of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah and addresses a key practical issue: the validity of praying behind a Muslim who commits major sins. By understanding these conditions, you will see how Hanafi scholars maintained unity and avoided excommunication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ten conditions
List each condition as explicitly stated in the passage: affirming uncreated Qur'an, praying behind any imam, predestination, wiping over socks, not rebelling, preferring the four caliphs, not excommunicating for sin, praying over deceased Muslims, and valuing congregational unity.
2
Understand the fitrah hadith explanation
Grasp the Hanafi interpretation that every child is born with innate disposition to recognize God, and parents influence religion without actual faith or disbelief from the child.
This underpins the principle that children follow parents in worldly rulings.
3
Resolve contradictory hadiths on praying behind sinners and treating Qadariyyah
The severe warnings against Qadariyyah applied to the early period of Islamic unity; after the assassination of Uthman, scholars like Ali continued to interact with people of desires, and prayer behind them remained valid.
This shows contextualization (takhsis bi al-‘urf) in Hanafi methodology.
4
Apply the ruling on prayer behind a fajir
As long as the imam is Muslim (even if sinful), prayer behind him is valid. Only those whose beliefs constitute kufr (e.g., denying predestination or uncreated Qur'an) invalidate prayer.
The principle is 'la yakhruju ahad min al-Islam bi dhanb'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
خلفاً
شيئاً في الله تعالى لا يليق بصفاته. والثاني يقر بأن القرآن كلام الله تعالى وليس بمخلوق . والثالث يرى الجمعة والعيدين خلف كل بر وفاجر والرابع يرى القدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى. والخامس يرى المسح على الخفين جائزاً. والسادس لا يخرج على الأمير بالسيف. والسابع يفضل أبا بكر وعمر وعثمان وعلياً على سائر الصحابة والثامن لا يكفر أحداً من أهل القبلة بذنب والتاسع يصلي على من مات من أهل القبلة العاشر يرى الجماعة رحمة والفرقة عذاباً. قال صاحب الكشاف في هذا الفصل شروط وزيادات لأصحابنا يجب أن تراعى. وسئل أبو النصر الدبوسي عن معنى قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «كل مولود يولد على الفطرة» قال : أي يولد على دلالة الخلقة على معنى أن الله تعالى خلقه على خلقة لو نظر إليها وتفكر فيها على حسب ما يجب لدلته على ربوبيته ووحدانيته. ومعنى قوله «يهودانه» أي ينقلانه إلى حكم اليهودية وأحوالها بالتلقين لكونه في أيديهم لذلك ظهر العمل في المسألتين عن سلف أن الولد يكون تابعاً للوالدين من غير من أن يكون منه كفر أو إسلام على الحقيقة. وسئل أبو النصر الدبوسي فقيل : ما معنى الأخبار التي رويت عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وروي في بعضها صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر وفي بعضها القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة إن مرضوا فلا تعودوهم وإن ماتوا فلا تشيعوا جنائزهم وفي بعضها إن أمتي ستفترق على كذا وكذا كلهم في النار إلا واحدة فقال المشايخ: إن من شرائط السنة والجماعة أن لا يكفر أحد من أهل القبلة. وسئل بعضهم عن الفاجر والبر فقال : الفاجر هو الفاسق من أهل الإسلام. العدل هو من أهل الإسلام وقد جاء مفسراً عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «لا يخرج أحد من أهل الإسلام بذنب وذكر افتراق الأديان بالأهواء فمن كان من أهل الإسلام فالصلاة خلفه جائزة وإن كان يعلم الكبائر وأهل الأهواء على ضربين منهم من يخرج عن الإسلام، لا ومنهم من يخرج. فمن خرج عن الإسلام لا تجوز الصلاة خلفه وقد سبق الكلام فيه مستوفى في تتمة كلمات الكفر في آخر كلمات الكفر في آخر كتاب السير وفي باب الجماعة : ومن لا يخرج منه فالصلاة خلفه جائزة، ومن خرج من الإسلام فهو في النار خالد، ومن لم يخرج منه فهو في جملة أهل المشيئة قال الله تعالى إن الله لا يغفر أن يشرك به ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمن يشاء [النساء : ٤٨] وأما ما جاء في حق أهل الأهواء أنهم لا يعادون ولا تشيع
والبر
جنائزهم فهذا تغليظ وتشديد كان في الزمان الأول حيث كان المسلمون أمة واحدة في عهد أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان وعلي رضي الله تعالى عنهم أجمعين ولما قتل عثمان وقعت الفرقة وظهرت الأهواء وغلبت الأحزاب أهل الأهواء ولم يمكن إمضاء الأمر على السبيل الأول وقد كانوا يجالسون علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه ويزاحمون، وكذا العلماء والفقهاء من بعده إلى يومنا هذا، والدليل على ذلك ما جاء أن شهادة أهل الأهواء جائزة، وسئل أبو بكر القاضي عن الرجل هل يعلم أنه على مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة فقال : إذا رجع علمه إلى كتاب الله وإلى ما قاله السلف الصالح فهو على مذهب السنة والجماعة .
Book of Disliked Acts. ...something... in God Almighty that is not befitting His attributes. The second affirms that the Qur'an is the speech of God Almighty and is not created. The third holds that Friday and Eid prayers are offered behind every righteous person and sinner. The fourth holds that capacity for good and evil is from God Almighty. The fifth holds that wiping over socks is permissible. The sixth does not rebel against the ruler with the sword. The seventh prefers Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali over the rest of the Companions. The eighth does not excommunicate anyone of the people of the qibla for a sin. The ninth prays over whoever dies of the people of the qibla. The tenth holds that congregation is mercy and disunity is punishment. The author of al-Kashshaf said in this chapter: there are conditions and additions for our companions that must be observed. Abu al-Nasr al-Dabusi was asked about the meaning of his saying, peace be upon him, 'Every child is born upon the fitrah.' He said: He is born upon the indication of creation, meaning that God Almighty created him with a nature that, if he looked at it and reflected upon it as required, would guide him to His lordship and oneness. And the meaning of his saying, 'his parents make him a Jew' is that they transfer him to the rule of Judaism and its states by instruction because he is in their hands. Therefore, the practice in the two issues from the predecessors is that the child follows the parents without actual disbelief or Islam from him. Abu al-Nasr al-Dabusi was asked: What is the meaning of the reports narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him – in some of them: 'Pray behind every righteous person and sinner,' and in some: 'The Qadariyyah are the Magians of this nation; if they are sick do not visit them, and if they die do not follow their funerals,' and in some: 'My nation will split into so-and-so, all in the Fire except one.' The scholars said: Among the conditions of the Sunnah and the Community is that no one of the people of the qibla is excommunicated. Some of them were asked about the sinner and the righteous. He said: The sinner is the corrupt person from the people of Islam. The righteous is from the people of Islam. And it has come interpreted from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, 'No one from the people of Islam leaves Islam due to a sin.' And he mentioned the division of religions by desires. So whoever is from the people of Islam, prayer behind him is permissible even if he commits major sins. And the people of desires are of two types: some exit Islam and some do not. Whoever exits Islam, prayer behind him is not permissible. The discussion on this has already been covered in detail in the conclusion of words of disbelief at the end of the Book of Siyar and in the Chapter on Congregation. And whoever does not exit Islam, prayer behind him is permissible. Whoever exits Islam is in the Fire eternally, and whoever does not exit is included among the people of the will. Allah says: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [4:48]. As for what came regarding the people of desires – that they are not visited nor are their funerals followed – this was severity and strictness in the first era when the Muslims were one nation in the time of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them all. When Uthman was killed, division occurred and desires appeared, and the parties of the people of desires prevailed, and it was not possible to carry out the matter on the first path. They used to sit with Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, and crowd around him, and similarly the scholars and jurists after him until our day. The evidence for that is that the testimony of the people of desires is permissible. Abu Bakr al-Qadi was asked about a man: Does he know that he is upon the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah? He said: If his knowledge returns to the Book of Allah and to what the pious predecessors said, then he is upon the madhhab of the Sunnah and the Community.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the defining beliefs and actions of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, as well as the ruling on praying behind a sinful person. It begins by listing ten conditions that a person must uphold to be considered from Ahl al-Sunnah. These include affirming that the Qur'an is uncreated, offering Friday and Eid prayers behind any Muslim ruler, believing in divine predestination, wiping over socks, not rebelling against the ruler, preferring the four rightly guided caliphs, not excommunicating sinners, praying over deceased Muslims, and valuing congregational unity. Then it discusses a hadith about every child being born upon fitrah, explaining that fitrah means the innate disposition to recognize God's lordship, and that parents influence the child's religion without the child itself having actual faith or disbelief. This is a key Hanafi principle. Next, it resolves apparent contradictions among hadiths regarding praying behind sinful rulers and the treatment of the Qadariyyah. The explanation is that the severe warnings applied to the early period of Islamic unity, but after the assassination of Uthman and the rise of divisions, scholars like Ali and later jurists continued to pray behind sinful Muslims and considered their testimony valid. The passage concludes that a person is considered upon the Sunnah if his knowledge is based on the Qur'an and the way of the salaf. This shows the Hanafi approach of maintaining community unity and not excommunicating Muslims despite major sins.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة (Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah): Those who adhere to the ten conditions listed: belief in uncreated Qur'an, predestination, praying behind any imam, not rebelling, etc.
الفاجر (al-fajir): A sinful Muslim who commits major sins but remains within the fold of Islam.
أهل الأهواء (ahl al-ahwa'): People of heretical desires who hold beliefs deviating from Ahl al-Sunnah but not necessarily reaching kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Prayer is valid only if the sin is not known to the congregation.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim does not leave Islam by committing major sins, and prayer behind a sinful imam is valid, preserving congregational unity.
